Brian Heater
Hardware Editor


Brian Heater is the Hardware Editor at TechCrunch. He worked for a number of leading tech publications, including Engadget, PCMag, Laptop, and Tech Times, where he served as the Managing Editor. His writing has appeared in Spin, Wired, Playboy, Entertainment Weekly, The Onion, Boing Boing, Publishers Weekly, The Daily Beast and various other publications. He hosts the weekly Boing Boing interview podcast RiYL, has appeared as a regular NPR contributor and shares his Queens apartment with a rabbit named Lucy.

Since Russian troops invaded Ukraine in late February, Delfast\u2019s top priority has been to see its Ukrainian team of 30 safely evacuated from the most dangerous parts of the country.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n When not focusing on sales, marketing, R&D and customer support, Delfast\u2019s smaller team of seven employees based in Los Angeles has been pleading with U.S. politicians and the European Commission to supply Ukraine with anti-aircraft missiles and fighter jets that could help Ukraine gain back some control over its air space, and, hopefully, put a stop to this war.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n Delfast\u2019s co-founders, Daniel Tonkopi and Serhiy Denysenko, say they have always believed in safeguarding the future. When they founded Delfast in 2014, originally as a delivery company, Tonkoply and Denysenko knew that providing couriers with green transportation options would be critical to the company\u2019s operations.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n \t \n\t\t \n\t\t\tThe most important thing for an entrepreneur, and in general for any leader, is to protect the team and be completely honest with them during a tough time.\t\t\t\t\t\t\tDaniel Tonkopi, co-founder of Delfast<\/cite>\n\t\t\t\t\t<\/blockquote>\n\t<\/div>\n\t<\/span><\/p>\n The founders soon realized that a bike with the power, range and battery life their couriers needed didn\u2019t exist, and so they set out to build one. In 2017, backed by a Kickstarter campaign that saw the company raise $165,000, the startup began manufacturing a bike to fit its needs \u2013 one that promptly <\/span>won the Guinness Book of World Records<\/span><\/a> for the greatest distance traveled on an electric motorbike on a single charge.<\/span><\/p>\n More recently, the Delfast Top 3.0 e-motorbike <\/span>won Forbes\u2019 fastest e-bike of the year<\/span><\/a> in 2022 after the company announced some serious <\/span>upgrades to the vehicle during CES<\/span><\/a>.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n We spoke with Delfast\u2019s co-founders to discuss what it\u2019s like running a startup during a war, how the startup is considering breaking into new business verticals, and the importance of always having a Plan B.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n The following interview, part of an ongoing series with founders who are building transportation companies, has been edited for length and clarity.\u00a0<\/span><\/i><\/p>\n Note: Serhiy Denysenko\u2019s answers were translated from Ukrainian by a member of Delfast\u2019s team for TechCrunch.\u00a0<\/span><\/i><\/p>\n TC: Serhiy, you’re on the ground in Kyiv. What’s your day-to-day like?<\/b><\/p>\n Denysenko: <\/b>Every morning starts with a check-in on Slack with all the colleagues. It\u2019s important to keep in touch and know that everyone is fine, or as fine as is possible right now.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n Besides my work as a COO, I\u2019ve been helping with volunteering, getting supplies and medicine to people, and this is something that pretty much every Ukrainian is now doing. I had my family relocated to Hungary, so I feel more or less safe, and I\u2019m just trying to work as much as possible and do my best in every possible area, whether that\u2019s supporting the company or supporting Ukraine in general.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n How are you managing your team through this crisis? What\u2019s changed?<\/b><\/p>\n Denysenko: <\/b>We got used to working remotely during Coronavirus times, so we have our task tracker, where everyone can see his or her task. Every Monday, we have an online Zoom meeting. Previously we only had these meetings at the executive level, but now during the war, we are gathering all together, just to see each other\u2019s faces and ask how they\u2019re doing, how\u2019s everyone feeling. Just to talk with everybody.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n <\/div>","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":" “Every morning starts with a check-in on Slack with all the colleagues. the robo-berry"},"content":{"rendered":" If you’ve never picked a raspberry, well, first of all that’s too bad, because a fresh raspberry is a beautiful thing. But second, and more immediately relevant in this case, you would not know that there is a technique to it that, surprisingly, robots aren’t super good at because they tend to be… crushy. But this robo-berry<\/a> designed by Swiss researchers could usher in a new era of gentle, automated robo-pickers.<\/p>\n The secret to picking a raspberry is to grip it just enough to get purchase and then pull it downwards off the little stem, apparently called the “receptacle,” which seems backwards. Seems simple \u2014 and it is, but only our hands are among the most sensitive and finely controlled constructions in the universe, the culmination of a hundred million years of evolution, outdone only by (I suspect) raccoons.<\/p>\n Robots simply don’t have the senses necessary to figure out the perfect technique for picking a berry. But what if it could communicate with the berry to better sense the forces involved and avoid either a a brutal crushing or humiliating failure-to-detach?<\/p> <\/div>\n That’s what Kai Junge, a PhD student at EPFL in Switzerland, aims to accomplish with this “sensorized raspberry,” a silicone and silicon replica berry that provides feedback to the picking machine, allowing it to learn to pick faster and better \u2014 and cleaner.<\/p>\n “It\u2019s an exciting dilemma for us as robotics engineers,” said professor Josie Hughes, who worked with Junge on the project. “The raspberry harvesting season is so short, and the fruit is so valuable, that wasting them simply isn’t an option. What’s more, the cost and logistical challenges of testing different options out in the field are prohibitive. That\u2019s why we decided to run our tests in the lab and develop a replica raspberry for training harvesting robots.”<\/p>\n Apparently the hard part comes just at the moment of detaching, when the force needed to grip the berry on the receptacle suddenly becomes overkill as the object goes from solid to hollow.<\/p>\n The replica berry has a fluidic sensor that tells the system how much compression is being experienced by the silicone drooplets, allowing the control model to learn how to adjust its grip as if the berry itself is telling it how much is too much.<\/p>\n You can see the berry in action below:<\/p>\n <\/iframe><\/span><\/p>\n<p>The team plans to present their work at RobotSoft in April. And once the raspberry question is decided, they may move on to other berries, tomatoes, grapes&#8230; even apricots. The future is looking fresh!<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>If you&#8217;ve never picked a raspberry, well, first of all that&#8217;s too bad, because a fresh raspberry is a beautiful thing. But second, and more immediately relevant in this case, you would not know that there is a technique to it that, surprisingly, robots aren&#8217;t super good at because they tend to be&#8230; crushy. -companies?tags=8191"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=8191"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=8191"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2292389,"date":"2022-03-31T11:55:17","date_gmt":"2022-03-31T18:55:17","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2292389"},"modified":"2022-03-31T17:57:31","modified_gmt":"2022-04-01T00:57:31","slug":"all-eyes-are-on-swvl-as-it-starts-trading-on-a-spac-combination","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/31\/all-eyes-are-on-swvl-as-it-starts-trading-on-a-spac-combination\/","title":{"rendered":"All eyes are on Swvl as it starts trading on a SPAC combination"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Mass transit and shared mobility provider <a href=\"https:\/\/www.swvl.com\/\">Swvl<\/a> went public today in <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">a landmark moment for Egyptian and Middle Eastern tech ecosystems<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. It\u2019s also a test for the company going public despite a market that\u2019s been unfriendly toward combinations with special purpose acquisition companies, or SPACs, of late.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The Egypt-born and Dubai-based company has listed its shares at $10 on the Nasdaq through a merger with U.S. women-led blank check company Queen\u2019s Gambit Growth Capital. The planned merger, which will see Swvl offer 20-30% of its total shares, was <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/07\/28\/egyptian-ride-sharing-company-swvl-plans-to-go-public-in-a-1-5b-spac-merger\/\">announced last July<\/a>.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Following closing, the combined company, now \u201cSwvl Holding Corp,\u201d will trade under GMBT and GMBTW today before switching to SWVL and SWVLW on April 1.<\/span><\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2292389\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Swvl is the first company launched from Africa and the second Middle Eastern company to list on the Nasdaq via a SPAC merger<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. Anghami, an Abu Dhabi-based music streaming platform, <a href=\"https:\/\/eg.linkedin.com\/in\/mostafa-kandil-57761032\">did so in February<\/a> when it listed with Vistas Media Acquisition at a $220 million valuation.<\/span><\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"Q5eMhyfACo\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/07\/28\/egyptian-ride-sharing-company-swvl-plans-to-go-public-in-a-1-5b-spac-merger\/\">Egyptian ride-sharing company Swvl plans to go public in a $1.5B SPAC merger<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Egyptian ride-sharing company Swvl plans to go public in a $1.5B SPAC merger&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/07\/28\/egyptian-ride-sharing-company-swvl-plans-to-go-public-in-a-1-5b-spac-merger\/embed\/#?secret=CnJTROn2h9#?secret=Q5eMhyfACo\" data-secret=\"Q5eMhyfACo\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Swvl raised $121.5 million in private investment in public equities (PIPE) for this transaction<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. The European Bank for Reconstruction and Development (EBRD), Teklas Ventures, Chimera, Agility, and Luxor Capital Group are some of its other investors. The company is currently valued at $1.5 billion.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">In February, one of its investors, Atalaya Capital, pulled out of the transaction. And in a filing, Queen\u2019s Gambit announced the termination of forward <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">purchase<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> agreements worth $100 million in SPAC shares and an extra $2 million via a private placement.<\/span><\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">\u201cThe forward <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">purchase<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> agreement <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">was done<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> with a group, and it was <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">just<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> access to <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">additional<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> capital,\u201d Queen\u2019s Gambit Capital founder and CEO Victoria Grace told TechCrunch when asked if the termination affects the deal.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">\u201cIts termination doesn\u2019t affect the valuation of the company or anything around our fundamental deal, which is Queen\u2019s Gambit merging with SWVL, so the valuation [stays] the same,\u201d she said.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Investors withdrawing their interests and dollars from SPACs is not peculiar to Swvl. It\u2019s a usual occurrence &#8212; for instance, when BuzzFeed went public last December, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.wsj.com\/articles\/buzzfeed-suffers-wave-of-spac-investor-withdrawals-before-going-public-11638472756\">94% of the $287.5 million raised by the SPAC <\/a><\/span><a href=\"https:\/\/www.wsj.com\/articles\/buzzfeed-suffers-wave-of-spac-investor-withdrawals-before-going-public-11638472756\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">was withdrawn<\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> &#8212; particularly as the SPAC hype gives way in the face of an underperforming market and tighter regulation.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Despite the seeming setback, there\u2019s good news for Swvl. <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">According to CFO Youssef Salem, the company has an <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">additional $600 million from proceeds and<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> committed equity facility with B. Riley Principal to access over the next few weeks if certain conditions are met, he said.<\/span><\/p>\n<p>Swvl was founded by <a href=\"https:\/\/eg.linkedin.com\/in\/mostafa-kandil-57761032\">Mostafa Kandil<\/a>, Mahmoud Nouh and Ahmed Sabbah in 2017. The trio started the company as a bus-hailing service in Egypt and other ride-sharing services in emerging markets with fragmented public transportation.<\/p>\n<p>Its bus-hailing services enable users to make intra-state journeys by booking seats on buses running a fixed route. Swvl offerings have expanded beyond bus-hailing services, though. Now, the company offers inter-city rides, car ride-sharing, and corporate services in the 10 cities it operates in across Africa and the Middle East.<\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The partnership between Swvl and Queen\u2019s Gambit came from a mutual interest from both parties<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. <\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">While searching for a company to <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">acquire<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, Swvl fit the blank-check company\u2019s criteria: strong business fundamentals, mobility and logistics (one of its core verticals), and an ESG ethos around women and affordable transportation.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">On the other hand<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, Swvl &#8212; off the back of raising over $170 million in venture capital, expanding to over 16 countries across Latin America, Asia and Africa; hiring executives from Facebook, Uber and Optimus; and acquiring Shotl, Viapool and door2door &#8212; was on a quest for global dominance in the mobility space. <\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">A SPAC with Queen\u2019s Gambit was the most suitable option for it from a financial standpoint, and both parties feel strongly about the sustainability angle around transport &#8212; Swvl claims it has prevented approximately 289 million pounds of carbon emissions since its inception.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The company plans to expand into several countries over the next six months, including Colombia, Mexico, South Africa, and the U.S. <\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">In the meantime, all eyes will be on the company\u2019s performance as it <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">officially<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> starts trading tomorrow in a cooling SPAC market and a generally unsettled public market.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">\u201cThere\u2019s a softness in the market, but as long as the company operates and delivers results, <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">maybe<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> today, people don\u2019t pay attention to it, but they will in months ahead,\u201d Grace said about the worrying SPAC and public markets.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">\u201c<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">I think<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> the market will change <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">just<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> like it always does and people go back to fundamentals at how we look at company\u2019s performances. For Swvl, they have been beating every single number that was ever presented to us. And that\u2019s what makes me super excited about this. And that\u2019s the type of target you want to partner with.\u201d<\/span><\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"s9kBhwdIHM\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/08\/21\/almost-everything-you-need-to-know-about-spacs\/\">Almost everything you need to know about SPACs<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Almost everything you need to know about SPACs&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/08\/21\/almost-everything-you-need-to-know-about-spacs\/embed\/#?secret=dbGVg33T0n#?secret=s9kBhwdIHM\" data-secret=\"s9kBhwdIHM\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Mass transit and shared mobility provider Swvl went public today in a landmark moment for Egyptian and Middle Eastern tech ecosystems. /tc_video?tags=21691"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":576814951,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/corporate-services\/","name":"corporate services","slug":"corporate-services","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576814951"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576814951"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576814951"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576814951"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576814951"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":52630,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/dubai\/","name":"Dubai","slug":"dubai","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/52630"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=52630"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=52630"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=52630"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=52630"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2292372,"date":"2022-03-31T12:05:44","date_gmt":"2022-03-31T19:05:44","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2292372"},"modified":"2022-03-31T13:58:42","modified_gmt":"2022-03-31T20:58:42","slug":"microsoft-acquires-process-mining-vendor-minit-to-grow-its-automation-offerings","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/31\/microsoft-acquires-process-mining-vendor-minit-to-grow-its-automation-offerings\/","title":{"rendered":"Microsoft acquires process mining vendor Minit to grow its automation offerings"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Signaling its ambitions in the process automation market, Microsoft has acquired <a href=\"https:\/\/www.minit.io\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Minit<\/a>, a Bratislava, Slovakia-originated process mining technology vendor, for an undisclosed sum, the companies announced today. Microsoft says that the purchase will &#8220;further empower&#8221; it to &#8220;help &#8230; customers digitally transform&#8221; by creating a more complete picture of their processes &#8212; and identifying which of those processes are ripe for automation.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Minit currently enables businesses to transform the way they analyze, monitor and optimize their processes. Minit\u2019s solutions have helped businesses gain deep insights into how processes run, uncover root causes of operational challenges and help mitigate undesired process outcomes,&#8221; Justin Graham, Microsoft&#8217;s general manager of process insights, wrote in a <a href=\"https:\/\/blogs.microsoft.com\/blog\/2022\/03\/31\/microsoft-acquires-minit-to-strengthen-process-mining-capabilities\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">post<\/a> on Microsoft&#8217;s corporate blog. &#8220;[With Minit, our] customers will be able to better understand their process data, uncover what operations look like in reality, and drive process standardization and improvement across the entire organization to ensure compliance at every step.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>Microsoft dipped its toes into process mining with the launch of new features in Power Automate in 2019 and the acquisition of Softomotive, an RPA software provider, a year later. But with Minit, the tech giant is doubling down on a software category that could be worth over $11 billion by 2030, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.wfmz.com\/news\/pr_newswire\/pr_newswire_technology\/global-process-mining-software-market-size-value-estimated-to-reach-usd-11-096-7-million\/article_a95b3354-ec2f-5389-b761-e4dbbdadbb97.html#:~:text=According%20to%20research%20report%20published,forecast%20period%202022%20to%202030.\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">according<\/a> to a report from Polaris Market Research.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2292372\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>It wasn&#8217;t immediately clear whether the whole of the Minit team will join Microsoft &#8212; or, indeed, whether the company will remain spread across its current locations. (Minit is now headquartered in Amsterdam, with satellite offices in London and New York.) But CEO James Dening said that customers shouldn&#8217;t expect a change in the level of support they&#8217;re currently receiving.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;We are looking forward to what it means to become part of an industry leader like Microsoft and what that brings us &#8212; how we can use that scale and excellence to continue to deliver great solutions to our customers,&#8221; Dening wrote in a blog <a href=\"https:\/\/www.minit.io\/blog\/microsoft-minit-acquisition\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">post<\/a> on Minit&#8217;s website. &#8220;It has been a privilege to lead the company for the last year, and I\u2019m excited to continue my journey with the team, as part of what I consider to be the world\u2019s leading software company.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>In a statement, Microsoft spokesperson Zara Huang told TechCrunch that the Minit team will move into the\u00a0<span class=\"il\">Microsoft<\/span> Process Insights team and that there will be &#8220;no change&#8221; to the current work location of Minit team members. <span class=\"il\">Microsoft<\/span> is in early stages of determining how Minit will be integrated into its offerings, she said, and the companies will share more details when they&#8217;re available.<\/p>\n<p>Minit, which was founded in 2015 by Rasto Hlavac and had raised \u20ac10.3 million (~$11.40 million) prior to the acquisition, is one of an expanding number of startups developing process mining tools aimed at enterprise clientele. Process mining, also known as task discovery, involves spotting root cause workflow issues and bottlenecks by pulling data from systems including desktop, email apps and workflows. It&#8217;s a key part of robotic process automation (RPA), a technology that promises to automate monotonous, repetitive tasks traditionally performed by human workers while at the same time generating logs to identify potential cost savings.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>As Protocol&#8217;s Aisha Counts <a href=\"https:\/\/www.protocol.com\/bulletins\/microsoft-process-mining-minit\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">notes<\/a>, process mining has traditionally been done by system integrators who map out processes by analyzing manual workflows. Process mining software is designed to digitize the approach in a way that reduces the expense, time and effort involved.<\/p>\n<p>Underlining the appetite for process mining technologies, Celonis, a data processing company, earlier this week acquired Minit competitor Process Analytics Factory, which coincidentally integrates with Microsoft&#8217;s Power BI analytics platform. Just in the past several years, RPA vendor Automation Anywhere acquired process discovery and mining startups FortressIQ, Process Gold\\ and StepShot; Blue Prism released a task mining solution called Capture; and rivals including ABBYY and Kryon have expanded their process mining offerings.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"2NKiKfcj0k\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/29\/celonis-pushes-into-microsoft-ecosystem-with-100m-process-analytics-factory-acquisition\/\">Celonis pushes into Microsoft ecosystem with $100M Process Analytics Factory acquisition<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Celonis pushes into Microsoft ecosystem with $100M Process Analytics Factory acquisition&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/29\/celonis-pushes-into-microsoft-ecosystem-with-100m-process-analytics-factory-acquisition\/embed\/#?secret=wqSRCOP7wQ#?secret=2NKiKfcj0k\" data-secret=\"2NKiKfcj0k\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p>&#8220;You know the process space is hot when even Microsoft, with its vast resources, has to buy its way in. I\u2019m sure Microsoft is seeing the same trends that we saw, which drove the combination of FortressIQ and Automation Anywhere,&#8221; Pankaj Chowdhry, EVP of discovery at Automation Anywhere and formerly CEO of FortressIQ, told TechCrunch via email. &#8220;Customers are starved for process data to help them navigate their transformation journeys and any vendor that doesn&#8217;t have best-in-class process capabilities will find itself challenged to offer a compelling solution to their customers.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>Microsoft&#8217;s Minit acquisition comes at a time when the broader business process automation industry, which remains <a href=\"https:\/\/news.crunchbase.com\/news\/robotic-automation-is-back\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">flush with cash<\/a>, heads toward general consolidation. SAP acquired German process automation company Signavio in January 2021, just before ServiceNow got into the RPA segment with the buyout of India-based Intellibot.io. IBM <a href=\"https:\/\/newsroom.ibm.com\/2021-04-15-IBM-to-Acquire-myInvenio-to-help-Organizations-Use-AI-powered-Automation-to-Better-Streamline-Business-Processes\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">acquired<\/a> process mining software company MyInvenio in April. And Salesforce\u2019s MuleSoft and Microsoft followed suit with the purchases of automation tech providers <a href=\"https:\/\/venturebeat.com\/2021\/08\/02\/mulesoft-acquires-rpa-provider-servicetrace\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Servicetrace<\/a>\u00a0and\u00a0<a href=\"https:\/\/venturebeat.com\/2021\/10\/22\/microsoft-acquires-clear-software-to-strengthen-process-automation-offerings\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Clear Software<\/a>, respectively.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Process mining, discovery and task mining has seen a lot of transformation with many acquisitions in the last year. [It] now appears to be maturing as a market and becoming commoditized under major automation platforms,&#8221; Saikat Ray, Gartner senior research director, told TechCrunch via email. &#8220;Gartner sees an emergence of automation platform vendors offering process mining and task mining as embedded capabilities, along with RPA.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p><em>Updated at 4:15 p.m. ET, March 31, with quotes from Microsoft and Automation Anywhere.<\/em><\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Signaling its ambitions in the process automation market, Microsoft has acquired Minit, a Bratislava, Slovakia-originated process mining technology vendor, for an undisclosed sum, the companies announced today. Microsoft says that the purchase will &#8220;further empower&#8221; it to &#8220;help &#8230; customers digitally transform&#8221; by creating a more complete picture of their processes &#8212; and identifying which automation","slug":"robotic-process-automation","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/449560943"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=449560943"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=449560943"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=449560943"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=449560943"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":576598619,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/rpa\/","name":"RPA","slug":"rpa","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576598619"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576598619"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576598619"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576598619"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576598619"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":6,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/technology\/","name":"technology","slug":"technology","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/6"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=6"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=6"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=6"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=6"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2292473,"date":"2022-03-31T14:10:50","date_gmt":"2022-03-31T21:10:50","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2292473"},"modified":"2022-03-31T14:10:57","modified_gmt":"2022-03-31T21:10:57","slug":"better-learning-through-complex-dough-manipulation","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/31\/better-learning-through-complex-dough-manipulation\/","title":{"rendered":"Better learning through &#8216;complex dough-manipulation&#8217;"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">A disproportionate number of the early industrial food-making robots we\u2019ve seen have been <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/05\/20\/robotics-roundup-12\/\">focused on pizza<\/a>. I\u2019ve long posited that this is for two key reasons. First: People like pizza. We eat a lot of it. Americans alone eat three billion pizzas a year. Second: It\u2019s relatively easy to make. The dough provides a fairly straightforward platform onto which ingredients are added.<\/p>\n<p>I say \u201cfairly\u201d here because there are still complications. There\u2019s really no such thing as easy when it comes to building robots that can execute variations on a task at a large scale. Here it\u2019s the dough that presents the problem. Turning a soft and malleable ball of dough into a pizza crust is one of those things humans have figured out how to do efficiently, but it still proves difficult for robot workers.<\/p>\n<p>A team of researchers at MIT, CMU and UC San Diego set out to create what they\u2019ve deemed \u201ccomplex dough-manipulation.\u201d The system is separated into a two-step process, in which the robot must first determine the task and then execute it using a tool like a rolling pin. The system, <a href=\"https:\/\/news.mit.edu\/2022\/robotic-deformable-object-0331\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">DiffSkill<\/a>, involves teaching robots complex tasks in simulations.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2292473\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>MIT notes:<\/p>\n<blockquote><p>A \u201cteacher\u201d algorithm solves each step the robot must take to complete the task. Then, it trains a \u201cstudent\u201d machine-learning model that learns abstract ideas about when and how to execute each skill it needs during the task, like using a rolling pin. With this knowledge, the system reasons about how to execute the skills to complete the entire task.<\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p>The researchers say the system outperformed those trained in the more traditional reinforcement learning model. \u201cOur framework provides a novel way for robots to acquire new skills. These skills can then be chained to solve more complex tasks which are beyond the capability of previous robot systems,\u201d says CSAIL grad student, Yunzhu Li.<\/p>\n<p>This is robotics, so the whole pizza thing is really an initial problem for a system designed to tackle a lot more tasks. The company points to the emerging field of eldercare robotics as a possible use going forward.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>A disproportionate number of the early industrial food-making robots we\u2019ve seen have been focused on pizza. I\u2019ve long posited that this is for two key reasons. First: People like pizza. We eat a lot of it. Americans alone eat three billion pizzas a year. Second: It\u2019s relatively easy to make. The dough provides a fairly Link","children":[]}]},"entities":{"posts":[{"id":2288103,"date":"2022-03-23T08:00:37","date_gmt":"2022-03-23T15:00:37","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2288103"},"modified":"2022-03-23T07:54:37","modified_gmt":"2022-03-23T14:54:37","slug":"ruggeds-construction-layout-robots-land-9-4m","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/23\/ruggeds-construction-layout-robots-land-9-4m\/","title":{"rendered":"Rugged\u2019s construction layout robots land $9.4M"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">It\u2019s been a little less than a year since we first <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/08\/30\/rugged-showcases-its-layout-printing-construction-robots\/\">noted Rugged Robotics<\/a>. The Houston-based startup developed a robot that prints building layouts on the floor of construction sites, so workers know where &#8212; and where not &#8212; to build. The \u201clayout Roomba,\u201d as the company puts it. At the time, the company had raised $2.5 million, by way of a 2019 round.<\/p>\n<p>Of course, that was before the great pandemic automation acceleration that\u2019s occurred in the intervening two to three years. Now, it seems, construction is a prime target for robotics. Pandemics happen, people get sick &#8212; but construction, it seems, never stops. Rugged\u2019s tech isn\u2019t designed to replace humans on the job site, but rather to increase accuracy &#8212; but even so, it seems the firm is benefiting from increased interest.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2288106\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2288106\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2288106\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Leo4-Dallas.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"683\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Leo4-Dallas.jpg 4032w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Leo4-Dallas.jpg?resize=150,100 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Leo4-Dallas.jpg?resize=300,200 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Leo4-Dallas.jpg?resize=768,512 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Leo4-Dallas.jpg?resize=680,453 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Leo4-Dallas.jpg?resize=1536,1024 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Leo4-Dallas.jpg?resize=2048,1365 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Leo4-Dallas.jpg?resize=50,33 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2288106\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Paul Valle \/ Rugged<\/p><\/div><\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2288103\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>Today, it marks a Series A that brings $9.4 million in funding, courtesy of BOLD Capital Partners and Brick &amp; Mortar Ventures, along with Riot Ventures, Morpheus , Embark, Consigli Construction Company and Suffolk Technologies. The latest round brings the company\u2019s full funding to around $12 million to date.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cWe set out to modernize the construction industry, and to build practical solutions that solve the pain points contractors struggle with every day,\u201d CEO Derrick Morse said in a release. \u201cWe believe that layout is the ideal starting point. Layout is the beachhead for construction automation. It sits at the intersection of the digital and physical world, solves a huge problem, and unlocks the ability to deploy robotics onto job sites in a very meaningful way.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>The new round of funding will go toward accelerating the robot\u2019s deployment, as well as making additional hires. Most recently, the startup brought on Auris Health\u2019s Mason Markee. The startup joins a number of other field printers, including Dusty, which raised its own $16.5 million Series A last summer. Rugged says it&#8217;s looking to distinguish itself by way of a &#8220;self-contained solution,&#8221; which requires minimal setup and allows for multiple robots to operate at once.<\/p>\n<p>The firm is also building toward more autonomy. It notes, &#8220;<span style=\"font-size: 1rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\">As Rugged Robotics further refines its end-to-end system, the company plans to simplify deployment and eventually unlock unmanned, overnight work.&#8221;<\/span><\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>It\u2019s been a little less than a year since we first noted Rugged Robotics. The Houston-based startup developed a robot that prints building layouts on the floor of construction sites, so workers know where &#8212; and where not &#8212; to build. The \u201clayout Roomba,\u201d as the company puts it. robotics","slug":"rugged-robotics","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576914728"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576914728"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576914728"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576914728"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576914728"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":449557042,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/startups\/","name":"Startups","slug":"startups","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/449557042"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=449557042"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=449557042"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=449557042"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=449557042"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2287499,"date":"2022-03-23T07:30:54","date_gmt":"2022-03-23T14:30:54","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2287499"},"modified":"2022-03-23T07:32:56","modified_gmt":"2022-03-23T14:32:56","slug":"nothings-first-phone-will-be-released-this-summer","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/23\/nothings-first-phone-will-be-released-this-summer\/","title":{"rendered":"Nothing\u2019s first phone will be released this summer"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Say what you will &#8212; Nothing knows how to tease a teaser. In the hardware startup\u2019s defense, it noted that <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/09\/money-for-nothing-and-chips-from-a-series-b\/\">this morning\u2019s event<\/a> would be a \u201croadmap\u201d reveal, specifically referring to another device coming to its lineup, without offering much in the way of information on said product. The company has, however, confirmed the much-rumored arrival of its second hardware offering, the Nothing Phone (1).<\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/02\/nothing-smartphone-carl-pei\/\">We confirmed the device\u2019s existence<\/a> earlier this month, noting that founder Carl Pei had been taking meetings with high-ranking executives at Mobile World Congress, where he showed off a version of the device that features a similarly transparent design as its Ear (1) headphones.<\/p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-2288355\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Lock-Screen-First-Iteration-not-final.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"576\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Lock-Screen-First-Iteration-not-final.jpg 1920w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Lock-Screen-First-Iteration-not-final.jpg?resize=150,84 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Lock-Screen-First-Iteration-not-final.jpg?resize=300,169 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Lock-Screen-First-Iteration-not-final.jpg?resize=768,432 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Lock-Screen-First-Iteration-not-final.jpg?resize=680,383 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Lock-Screen-First-Iteration-not-final.jpg?resize=1536,864 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Lock-Screen-First-Iteration-not-final.jpg?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2287499\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>Today the company offered a handful of additional details, adding that the product will feature a Snapdragon chip &#8212; no surprise there, really, given that Qualcomm is among Nothing\u2019s backers. Similar to OnePlus, another Pei-founded company, the device will sport its own custom take on Android, Nothing OS, which it says is \u201cbuilt on an open and seamless ecosystem that will effortlessly connect and integrate Nothing products and products from other world-leading brands.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>Ecosystem has always been at the heart of Nothing\u2019s play, so it will be interesting to see precisely how that integration looks. No doubt the company imagines the phone will serve as the hub of that system, in much the same way Apple, Samsung and the like envision their respective mobile-centric solar systems. Nothing says it\u2019s going to offer a preview of the operating system next month.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2288362\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2288362\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2288362\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-23-at-10.23.07-AM.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"592\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-23-at-10.23.07-AM.png 2318w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-23-at-10.23.07-AM.png?resize=150,87 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-23-at-10.23.07-AM.png?resize=300,173 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-23-at-10.23.07-AM.png?resize=768,444 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-23-at-10.23.07-AM.png?resize=680,393 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-23-at-10.23.07-AM.png?resize=1536,888 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-23-at-10.23.07-AM.png?resize=2048,1184 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-23-at-10.23.07-AM.png?resize=50,29 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2288362\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Nothing<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>The software sounds similar to what OnePlus has been working to offering with OxygenOS &#8212; tweaks to Android, without adding too much additional software. Aesthetically, it will be in keeping with the company&#8217;s &#8220;analog&#8221; design language. The company is attempting to walk the Apple path by developing the OS layer along with its hardware (albeit on top of Android). Its headphones will be immediately supported, and Pei says the firm is working on support for third-party products, including AirPods and cars like Tesla.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>Nothing is promising three years of operating system updates for the phone, as well as four years of security updates.<\/p>\n<p>Accordingly, it\u2019s going to follow the pattern established by the Ear (1) and portion out more information on the upcoming phone in the coming months.<\/p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-2288356\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Widgets-First-Iteration-not-final.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"576\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Widgets-First-Iteration-not-final.jpg 1920w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Widgets-First-Iteration-not-final.jpg?resize=150,84 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Widgets-First-Iteration-not-final.jpg?resize=300,169 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Widgets-First-Iteration-not-final.jpg?resize=768,432 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Widgets-First-Iteration-not-final.jpg?resize=680,383 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Widgets-First-Iteration-not-final.jpg?resize=1536,864 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Widgets-First-Iteration-not-final.jpg?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><\/p>\n<p>Along with the phone news, the company also announced that it\u2019s going back to the well with more crowdfunded equity, following a $70 million <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/09\/money-for-nothing-and-chips-from-a-series-b\/\">Series B<\/a> a mere two weeks ago. This time out, it\u2019s seeking $10 million, at the same valuation as that VC-backed round. It\u2019s opening preregistration now and officially opening things up April 5. It\u2019s been a winning strategy for the firm thus far, as it seeks to foster community involvement by giving fans a financial stake in its success.<\/p>\n<p>The device arrives at a tough &#8212; but hopeful time for mobile startups. Interest in handsets has waned, 15 years after the release of the first iPhone. Sales were leveling off and dipping prior to the pandemic, though that &#8212; along with subsequent supply chain constraints and chip shortages &#8212; have only exacerbated these trends. One-time major players like LG and HTC have either move away from the industry entirely or dramatically scaled back.<\/p>\n<p>Nothing joins a small movement of new mobile startups that also includes the privacy-focused <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/03\/osom-talks-its-first-phone-ahead-of-a-q4-release\/\">OSOM<\/a>, which was born from the fallout of Essential&#8217;s failure. Pei and Nothing, incidentally, purchased Essential IP, though the company has ultimately done nothing with the name.<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Say what you will &#8212; Nothing knows how to tease a teaser. "}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=24435"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=24435"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=24435"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=24435"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2288338,"date":"2022-03-23T07:13:52","date_gmt":"2022-03-23T14:13:52","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2288338"},"modified":"2022-03-23T09:44:48","modified_gmt":"2022-03-23T16:44:48","slug":"snap-buys-mind-controlled-headband-maker-nextmind","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/23\/snap-buys-mind-controlled-headband-maker-nextmind\/","title":{"rendered":"Snap buys mind-controlled headband maker, NextMind"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Snap this morning <a href=\"https:\/\/newsroom.snap.com\/welcome-nextmind\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">confirmed that it has acquired NextMind<\/a> for an undisclosed sum. The Paris-based startup is best known for its self-titled controller, which utilizes brain signals to move images on a PC interface. After announcing a $399 dev kit at CES, the company began shipping in Q2 2020. <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/12\/21\/nextminds-dev-kit-for-mind-controlled-computing-offers-a-rare-wow-factor-in-tech\/\">We took it for a spin<\/a> at the end of that year and called the hardware a \u201crare \u2018wow\u2019 factor.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>\u201cNextMind has joined Snap to help drive long-term augmented reality research efforts within Snap Lab,\u201d the company wrote in a blog post. \u201cSpectacles are an evolving, iterative research and development project, and the latest generation is designed to support developers as they explore the technical bounds of augmented reality.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>The news finds the firm integrating into Snap Lab, the social media company\u2019s hardware research wing. It also marks the end of NextMind\u2019s dev kit as a standalone. Pieces of the technology will almost certainly make their way into future Snap products, including AR plays like Camera and <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/05\/20\/snap-announces-its-latest-generation-of-its-spectacles-a-streamlined-device-for-experience-the-world-in-ar\/\">Spectacles<\/a>.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2288338\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>Founded in 2017 by a team of neuroscientists and hardware engineers, the company\u2019s technology utilizes a wearable headband with a built-in electroencephalogram to detect and read neural activity in the cortex. As the wearer views an image on a display, the headset can determine they want to move it. Mind-controlled interfaces like this make a lot of sense for augmented realty. Head-mounted displays, in particular, have long suffered from a controller problem, which such technologies could go a ways toward solving.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cThis technology monitors neural activity to understand your intent when interacting with a computing interface, allowing you to push a virtual button simply by focusing on it,\u201d Snap adds. \u201cThis technology does not &#8216;read&#8217; thoughts or send any signals towards the brain.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>NextMind\u2019s raised a $4.6 million seed round in mid-2018. The team will continue to work out of Paris, with 20 of its employees (largely technical) joining Snap Labs, and focusing on longer-term research and development. <span style=\"font-size: 1rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\">Last May, Snap<\/span><a style=\"background-color: #ffffff; font-size: 1rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\" href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/05\/21\/snap-acquires-ar-startup-waveoptics-which-provides-tech-for-spectacles-for-over-500m\/\"> purchased WaveOptics<\/a><span style=\"font-size: 1rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\">, which makes components used in AR headsets. That same month, the company<\/span><a style=\"background-color: #ffffff; font-size: 1rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\" href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/05\/20\/snap-announces-its-latest-generation-of-its-spectacles-a-streamlined-device-for-experience-the-world-in-ar\/\"> previewed<\/a><span style=\"font-size: 1rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\"> its fourth-generation Spectacles, which it called the &#8220;first pair of glasses that bring augmented reality to life.&#8221;<\/span><\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"PBZUqUACPq\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/21\/3-factors-to-consider-when-adding-remote-visual-assistance-software-to-your-tech-stack\/\">3 factors to consider when adding remote visual assistance software to your tech stack<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;3 factors to consider when adding remote visual assistance software to your tech stack&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/21\/3-factors-to-consider-when-adding-remote-visual-assistance-software-to-your-tech-stack\/embed\/#?secret=K1KG1DvsWL#?secret=PBZUqUACPq\" data-secret=\"PBZUqUACPq\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Snap this morning confirmed that it has acquired NextMind for an undisclosed sum. The Paris-based startup is best known for its self-titled controller, which utilizes brain signals to move images on a PC interface. After announcing a $399 dev kit at CES, the company began shipping in Q2 2020. https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2287991"},"modified":"2022-03-22T12:22:04","modified_gmt":"2022-03-22T19:22:04","slug":"kickstarters-ceo-stepping-down-in-april","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/22\/kickstarters-ceo-stepping-down-in-april\/","title":{"rendered":"Kickstarter\u2019s CEO stepping down in April"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">In a<a href=\"https:\/\/www.kickstarter.com\/blog\/moving-forward-with-gratitude\"> blog post<\/a> today titled &#8220;Moving Forward, With Gratitude,&#8221; Kickstarter CEO Aziz Hasan announced that he is stepping down from his leadership role at the crowdfunding platform. After three years, April 4 will be his final day as chief executive. In his stead, the company\u2019s COO Sean Leow will fill the role as interim CEO as the company\u2019s board of directors searches for a more permanent replacement.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cI am so proud of the work we\u2019ve done together,\u201d Hasan writes. \u201cLeading such a passionate, skilled, and dedicated team through intense moments of change, milestone victories, and complex challenges has been a humbling and rewarding experience.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>The executive<a href=\"https:\/\/www.fastcompany.com\/90733608\/kickstarters-ceo-is-stepping-down-citing-personal-reflection\"> spoke with Fast Company<\/a> about the decision, citing \u201cpersonal reflection\u201d as a motivator, as well as a desire to spend more time with his young family. As Hasan notes, his tenure has seen strong growth for the service, though the last several years have also had their share of controversy.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2287991\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>In 2020, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/02\/18\/kickstarter-workers-vote-to-unionize\/\">Kickstarter staff voted to unionize<\/a>, a move Hasan had referred to as \u201cinherently adversarial\u201d in a letter to staff, adding,<\/p>\n<blockquote><p>That dynamic doesn\u2019t reflect who we are as a company, how we interact, how we make decisions, or where we need to go. We believe that in many ways it would set us back, and that the us vs. them binary already has.<\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p>More recently, it courted backlash among creators with plans to move its services to the blockchain. Amid fierce criticism, Kickstarter <a href=\"https:\/\/www.kickstarter.com\/articles\/we-won-t-make-changes-to-kickstarter-without-you\">promised to listen to user feedback<\/a> to \u201cbetter address [ \u2026 ] concerns.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>Leow highlighted Hasan\u2019s accomplishments in a statement,<\/p>\n<blockquote><p>Aziz poured so much of his creative spirit and expertise into Kickstarter over the past 3 years as CEO. We deeply appreciate his contributions and look forward to building on them as we aim to grow the number of creative projects that come to life. As a die-hard believer in the power of creative projects, I am committed to keep Kickstarter moving in the right direction as we search for our next leader.<\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p>Co-founder and former CEO Perry Chen echoed the sentiment, noting,<\/p>\n<blockquote><p>Aziz Hasan took over leadership of Kickstarter at a critical moment for the company, providing a thoughtful and steady hand throughout his tenure, including historic funding milestones for creative projects and navigating the many challenges of a global pandemic. While we search for the future CEO of Kickstarter, we are very fortunate to have Sean Leow leading the company. Sean has consistently led many of the company&#8217;s most important initiatives throughout his long tenure at Kickstarter and brings a deep expertise and passion for helping creative projects come to life.<\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p>Before joining Kickstarter, Leow was employed by Facebook and co-founded social media art site, Neocha.<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>In a blog post today titled &#8220;Moving Forward, With Gratitude,&#8221; Kickstarter CEO Aziz Hasan announced that he is stepping down from his leadership role at the crowdfunding platform. After three years, April 4 will be his final day as chief executive. In his stead, the company\u2019s COO Sean Leow will fill the role as interim new agtech robot enters the crop monitoring category"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">I\u2019ve suddenly found myself <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/17\/to-servi-man\/\">writing a lot about agtech of late<\/a>. Maybe it\u2019s because spring officially sprung over the weekend \u2013 or perhaps it\u2019s that pesky impending environmental collapse that\u2019s frequently top of mind.<\/p>\n<p>Whatever the case, I\u2019ve mostly been lamenting a general lack of traction among robotics in the category, so I\u2019m always happy to see a new contender emerge.<\/p>\n<p>A lot of this stuff is also probably top of mind given that the World Agri-Tech Summit is currently happening in San Francisco. Today at the event, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.growmark.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Growmark<\/a> and<a href=\"https:\/\/www.solinftec.com\/en-us\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"> Solinftec<\/a> announced a partnership set to bring an unnamed agtech robot to the market. The product is being field-tested for the remainder of the year, and the companies are planning\/hoping to bring it to market at some point in 2023.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2287706\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>The robot functions similarly to a number of products we\u2019ve seen attempting to address a potentially large market, including recent addition <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/22\/verdant-aims-to-be-the-robotic-king-of-carrot-weeders\/\">Verdant<\/a> and a bunch of startups John Deere keeps buying. It effectively rides around the field autonomously, scanning for things like crop health and nutrition, along with potential trouble areas like pests and weeds. That information is collated and sent to the farmer for action.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cWe\u2019re taking our robot directly to the fields for practical implications,\u201d Solinftec COO Daniel Padr\u00e3o said in a release. \u201cThis cutting-edge technology will help develop agricultural solutions and support sustainable farm practices. We are honored to have such a progressive partner as Growmark to move forward with this first launch as we continue to work together to support farmers on seizing the opportunities in agriculture.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>As a base-level functionality, I think this makes sense. Attempting to monitor vast swaths of land on a micro-level is extremely difficult work, and many times it means waiting for problem areas to balloon into actual problems before properly addressing them. There are a number of different angles being taken here, from robots to drones to satellite imaging. The companies are also competing with robotics that monitor crops while performing other functions, be it weeding, picking or plowing.<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>I\u2019ve suddenly found myself writing a lot about agtech of late. Maybe it\u2019s because spring officially sprung over the weekend \u2013 or perhaps it\u2019s that pesky impending environmental collapse that\u2019s frequently top of mind. Whatever the case, I\u2019ve mostly been lamenting a general lack of traction among robotics in the category, so I\u2019m always happy ],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576996978"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576996978"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576996978"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576996978"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2287457,"date":"2022-03-21T14:20:13","date_gmt":"2022-03-21T21:20:13","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2287457"},"modified":"2022-03-21T14:20:35","modified_gmt":"2022-03-21T21:20:35","slug":"with-9-3m-in-fresh-funding-zestworld-plans-a-newsletter-service-for-creator-owned-comics","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/21\/with-9-3m-in-fresh-funding-zestworld-plans-a-newsletter-service-for-creator-owned-comics\/","title":{"rendered":"With $9.3M in fresh funding, Zestworld plans a newsletter service for creator-owned comics"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">The comics world has seemingly been waiting for a digital revolution since the birth of the internet. Launched in 2007, ComiXology has come the closest to delivering such a play to the medium, so naturally, Amazon went and purchased the service and messed it up. Its most recent offering left subscribers in the lurch, finally leading the brand to admit that the integration \u201cprocess has been far from seamless,\u201d and promising to respond to user feedback.<\/p>\n<p>It is, indeed, not dissimilar from the blowback Kickstarter received following its big blockchain announcement late last year. That service has long been popular with creators, who felt alienated by its recent announcements. More recently, Substack has gotten into the comics, enlisting some big names, including Grant Morrison and Chip Zdarsky, though that service has not been without its share of controversy.<\/p>\n<p>Announced last year, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.zestworld.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Zestworld<\/a> is looking to take on the media with its own custom-built platform. Designed specifically for the comics medium, the service has already found a share of high-profile supporters, including Alexis Ohanian and Twitch\u2019s Kevin Lin.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2287457\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>\u201cThe current landscape for comic creators to publish their work digitally and connect with fans is abysmal,\u201d Ohanian said in a release. \u201cZestworld is bringing together every aspect of the comic creator business and community into one centralized platform that is disrupting how comic creators publish and own IP, as well as enabling fans to connect with creators directly in entirely novel ways.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>Both joined a Series A round led by General Catalyst that provides $9.37 million to deliver on the service\u2019s plans to give creators a comic-optimized newsletter platform, coupled with an IP management tool. IP has, of course, has long been the bread and butter for the mainstream comics industry. One can do all right selling comics at the highest levels, but let\u2019s be honest, licensing is where the money is really made here.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cFinding platforms that are creator-driven is a true challenge in comics, and what Zestworld offers is refreshing and transparent,\u201d said Alex Segura, one of the writers involved in the launch. \u201cZestworld allows creators like me to publish my work on my own schedule, customize benefits and the ways the creative team and I get to interact with my audience, and allows us to maintain full IP-rights ownership to everything we publish through the platform. It&#8217;s a hard deal to beat.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>Segura is joined by Amanda Conner, Jimmy Palmiotti, Peter J. Tomasi, Eric Canete and Phil Jimenez. Other promised features include community management and \u201cNFTs\/metaverse events,\u201d because one can\u2019t launch a service in 2022 without those things.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>The comics world has seemingly been waiting for a digital revolution since the birth of the internet. Launched in 2007, ComiXology has come the closest to delivering such a play to the medium, so naturally, Amazon went and purchased the service and messed it up. Its most recent offering left subscribers in the lurch, finally enterprise drone goes foldable"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">The first DJI Mavic turned the world of consumer drones on its head when it was released back in late-2016. The compact, foldable design launched a million copy cats around the world &#8212; including a number under the drone giant\u2019s own umbrella. Compact certainly isn\u2019t the first word that comes to mind in the enterprise space, however. Those designs tend to be far heavier and more robust than products designed to be stored in a photography backpack.<\/p>\n<p>Two years after the first model arrived, the company introduced enterprise capabilities <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2018\/10\/29\/dji-releases-a-modified-mavic-2-drone-aimed-at-enterprise\/\">for the Mavic 2<\/a>. The biggest change there was the addition of a modular mount that could be used to add on things like a spotlight and a speaker to help it fly in less than ideal conditions. But for all intents and purporses, the Mavic 2 Enterprise was still a consumer drone with some added work benefit.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2286814\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2286814\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2286814\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/DJI-M30-in-flight-1-1.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"683\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/DJI-M30-in-flight-1-1.jpg 9504w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/DJI-M30-in-flight-1-1.jpg?resize=150,100 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/DJI-M30-in-flight-1-1.jpg?resize=300,200 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/DJI-M30-in-flight-1-1.jpg?resize=768,512 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/DJI-M30-in-flight-1-1.jpg?resize=680,453 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/DJI-M30-in-flight-1-1.jpg?resize=1536,1024 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/DJI-M30-in-flight-1-1.jpg?resize=2048,1365 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/DJI-M30-in-flight-1-1.jpg?resize=50,33 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2286814\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> DJI<\/p><\/div><\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2286800\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>This morning, the company announced the Matrice 30, a purpose-built drone for enterprise applications that brings the Mavic\u2019s most prominent feature &#8212; folding arms &#8212; to the longstanding line. Once again, DJI is highlight that the system can be carried in a backpack &#8212; albeit a larger one than what\u2019s needed for the Mavic and its various derivative drones. The larger size assures a more robust design that\u2019s necessary for some of the conditions these products face. The on-board battery is rated at 41-minutes &#8212; which is five minutes less than the Mavic 3\u2019s.<\/p>\n<p>As for weather concerns, the new drone is rated IP55, and the company says it&#8217;s capable of operating in temperatures ranging from -4 to 122 degrees Fahrenheit. Keep in mind, these drones are designed to face some really rough settings for inspections so their human counterparts can keep out of harm\u2019s way.<\/p>\n<p>The new drone comes bundled with a remote and is available through DJI\u2019s <a href=\"https:\/\/www.dji.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">site<\/a>.<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>The first DJI Mavic turned the world of consumer drones on its head when it was released back in late-2016. The compact, foldable design launched a million copy cats around the world &#8212; including a number under the drone giant\u2019s own umbrella. Compact certainly isn\u2019t the first word that comes to mind in the enterprise gyms have reopened, but investors are still betting on Hydrow\u2019s home rower"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">The home fitness craze has, predictably, died down somewhat since the height of pandemic-fueled buying sprees. Category leader Peloton is <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/08\/peloton-ceo-steps-down-as-the-company-cuts-2800-jobs\/\">smarting from gym reopenings<\/a> (among lots of other things) in a major way. Still, connected fitness predates COVID-19, and it will (knock on wood) be here after the pandemic ends.<\/p>\n<p>Plenty of investors are still bullish on the category, which &#8212; like the work from home movement &#8212; still has life in it left. It also seems likely that while Peloton\u2019s woes have scrambled the industry\u2019s North Star, companies like Hydrow may ultimately benefit from those struggles. For one thing, it opens the field up to more players \u2014 and perhaps more importantly, no one is talking about the rumored Peloton home rowing machine anymore.<\/p>\n<p>That\u2019s no doubt been a collective sigh from the company and competitors like <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/07\/20\/cityrow-raises-12m-for-connected-rowing-machines-and-studios\/\">CityRow<\/a> and <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/08\/11\/gamified-home-rowing-machine-aviron-raises-4-5m\/\">Aviron<\/a>. Given Peloton\u2019s ramped-up production capacity and the amount of money it\u2019s already spent on content, it was well positioned to take the world of home rowers by storm.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2286239\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>Boston-based Hyrdow this week is getting a robust vote of confidence from investors, in the form of a $55 million Series D (or, \u201capproximately\u201d $55 million, per the language in a release). Founder and CEO Bruce Smith uses the word \u201chybrid\u201d in the release, which may well be a concession that home devices are destined to play a part of a larger workout that once again includes gyms.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2286242\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2286242\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2286242\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Mike_OnHydrow_Lifestyle_Scarlet_FF.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"675\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Hydrow<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>\u201cAs more and more people embrace a hybrid approach to fitness, we continue to see extraordinary adoption, and our top priority is ensuring we can keep meeting that demand,\u201d the executive says in a release. \u201cThis latest round of funding will not only allow us to do that, but will give us the opportunity to further invest in our product offering and drive innovation, so we can continue to deliver a best-in-class experience for our members.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>There\u2019s room for growth here, certainly. Home rowers don\u2019t have the saturation of treadmills or bikes, but by all accounts still offer a solid full body workout. Another point in their favor in the home setting is that they can be stored with (relatively) little space compared to treadmills. The company notes that it grew revenue 3x between 2020 and 2021 and now has north of 200,000 users. Of course, growth in that timeframe is likely not sustainable long term, given the current regression, but it\u2019s a great starting point for a company bursting onto the scene.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>The round was led by Constitution Capital and features L Catterton, RX3, Liberty Street, Activant Capital and Sandbridge Capital. It will be used to ramp up production and expand Hydrow\u2019s international footprint.<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>The home fitness craze has, predictably, died down somewhat since the height of pandemic-fueled buying sprees.
