":0,"rapidData":{"pt":"","pct":""},"submenu_categories":[],"_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/categories\/449223024"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/categories"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/category"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?categories=449223024"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?categories=449223024"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?categories=449223024"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":337,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/health\/","name":"Health","slug":"health","taxonomy":"category","parent":0,"rapidData":{"pt":"","pct":""},"submenu_categories":[],"_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/categories\/337"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/categories"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/category"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?categories=337"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?categories=337"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?categories=337"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[{"id":122639171,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/connected-fitness\/","name":"connected fitness","slug":"connected-fitness","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/122639171"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=122639171"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=122639171"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=122639171"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=122639171"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":576821491,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/home-fitness\/","name":"home fitness","slug":"home-fitness","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576821491"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576821491"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576821491"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576821491"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576821491"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2285449,"date":"2022-03-17T11:30:26","date_gmt":"2022-03-17T18:30:26","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2285449"},"modified":"2022-03-18T10:22:27","modified_gmt":"2022-03-18T17:22:27","slug":"to-servi-man","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/17\/to-servi-man\/","title":{"rendered":"To Servi man"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><span class=\"featured__span-first-words\">A nice secondary<\/span> effect of writing this newsletter is getting an influx of responses when I write on a specific topic. Last week it was agtech. I expressed a bit of disappointment in the category. So many robotics firms have either failed or been acquired. That\u2019s just kind of how it goes, here in robotics startupland, but there\u2019s so much room for potential in the category. The seeds have been planted, it\u2019s time to harvest.<\/p>\n<p>John Deere is well positioned to corner the market, through it\u2019s own footprint\/brand recognition, in-house research and a bunch of acquisitions. But come on, folks, it\u2019s food. I eat, you eat it. Farmers grown it, our bodies break it down and convert it into energy. Building blocks of life, people. You know the food pyramid? Everyone talks about grains this, fats that. Thing is, the whole thing is good.<\/p>\n<p>There\u2019s a lot of room for innovation, and many or most of the essential pieces are there: autonomous driving (in a far less risky setting than a city street), computer vision, machine learning, soft robotics grippers. Labor is in short supply and the average age of an American farmer is hovering around 58 years. I\u2019ve been getting a number of pitches after last week\u2019s Actuator, and it\u2019s great to see this stuff being deployed in fields for testing.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2285449\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2227841\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2227841\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout size-full wp-image-2227841\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/11\/Iron-Ox-Grover-Three-Quarter-View.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"683\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/11\/Iron-Ox-Grover-Three-Quarter-View.jpg 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/11\/Iron-Ox-Grover-Three-Quarter-View.jpg?resize=150,100 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/11\/Iron-Ox-Grover-Three-Quarter-View.jpg?resize=300,200 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/11\/Iron-Ox-Grover-Three-Quarter-View.jpg?resize=768,512 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/11\/Iron-Ox-Grover-Three-Quarter-View.jpg?resize=680,453 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/11\/Iron-Ox-Grover-Three-Quarter-View.jpg?resize=1536,1024 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/11\/Iron-Ox-Grover-Three-Quarter-View.jpg?resize=50,33 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2227841\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Iron OX<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>One piece of the puzzle I\u2019ve probably not given enough column space to is greenhouses. <a href=\"https:\/\/www.cuestaroble.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">A 2019 report<\/a> puts the total acres of U.S. greenhouse farming at 1,228,000. And, frankly, when it comes to greenhouse growing, the United States lags behind other markets, including the Netherlands, which has led the way for a few decades now. Like vertical farming, there are a number of reasons to be excited about the future of greenhouses, including sustainability and food security. And unlike many vertical farms, greenhouses draw direct energy from the sun.<\/p>\n<p>While it\u2019s true the category is a drop in the bucket compared to more traditional farming, I would be keeping a very close eye on things were I a roboticist. Remember that thing I said about having fewer potential risks deploying autonomy on a farm versus a city street? Well, greenhouses are an extremely controlled environment &#8212; something akin to the warehouse fulfillment category, in many cases with even fewer humans to navigate around.<\/p>\n<p>Iron Ox has received the most column ink (and raised a ton of money) in the category. The company\u2019s wheeled robots pick up and move trays of greens to address their needs, while a robotic arm harvest the crops. Other names include MetoMotion, which has developed a robotic picker. The Israeli firm <a href=\"https:\/\/www.prnewswire.com\/news-releases\/metomotion-closes-5-million-investment-led-by-ridder-and-navus-to-bring-robotic-automation-to-the-greenhouse-industry-301387497.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">closed a $5 round lateish last year.<\/a><\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2285126\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2285126\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout size-full wp-image-2285126\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-15-at-6.11.15-PM.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"511\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-15-at-6.11.15-PM.jpg 2262w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-15-at-6.11.15-PM.jpg?resize=150,75 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-15-at-6.11.15-PM.jpg?resize=300,150 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-15-at-6.11.15-PM.jpg?resize=768,383 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-15-at-6.11.15-PM.jpg?resize=680,339 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-15-at-6.11.15-PM.jpg?resize=1536,766 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-15-at-6.11.15-PM.jpg?resize=2048,1021 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-15-at-6.11.15-PM.jpg?resize=50,25 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2285126\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> IUNU<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>Earlier this week, I wrote about IUNU. It\u2019s not a great name &#8212; or even a particularly good one. It\u2019s pronounced \u201cyou knew\u201d somehow, and the startup\u2019s former \u201ciUNU\u201d stylization is now \u201cIUNU,\u201d all of which isn\u2019t particularly helped by the fact that it has a robot named \u201cLUNA.\u201d That said, LUNA is pretty neat, effectively running along a track on a greenhouse ceiling to get a bird\u2019s eye view of how plants are growing &#8212; and save farmers a lot of extra steps in the process. That, coupled with some of these picking robots paint a picture of more fully autonomous greenhouses in the future, if that\u2019s a route owners are looking to go.<\/p>\n<p>Meantime, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/16\/iunu-uses-robots-to-keep-an-eye-on-greenhouse-crops\/\">IUNU just raised $24 million<\/a>. \u201cThis round of investment reflects the confidence institutional investors have in us,\u201d CEO Adam Greenberg says in a release. \u201cThe conversation around autonomous growing has accelerated in the past year, and we\u2019re proud to be leading the way on this front.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>This week, the Stanford Institute for Human-Centered Artificial Intelligence (HAI) <a href=\"https:\/\/hai.stanford.edu\/news\/2022-ai-index-industrialization-ai-and-mounting-ethical-concerns\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">released its annual AI Index Report<\/a>. A couple of facts are relevant to our interests here. Quoting some bullets directly from an HAI blog post:<\/p>\n<blockquote>\n<ul>\n<li>Private investment in AI has more than doubled since 2020, in part due to larger funding rounds. In 2020, there were four funding rounds worth $500 million or more; in 2021, there were 15.<\/li>\n<li>AI has become more affordable and higher performing. The cost to train an image classification has decreased by 63.6% and training times have improved by 94.4% since 2018. The median price of robotic arms has also decreased fourfold in the past six years.<\/li>\n<li>The United States and China have dominated cross-country research collaborations on AI as the total number of AI publications continues to grow. The two countries had the greatest number of cross-country collaborations in AI papers in the last decade, producing 2.7 times more joint papers in 2021 than between the United Kingdom and China\u2014the second highest on the list.<\/li>\n<li>The number of AI patents filed has soared\u2014more than 30 times higher than in 2015, showing a compound annual growth rate of 76.9%.<\/li>\n<\/ul>\n<\/blockquote>\n<p>No shock, really, about the rate of interest &#8212; or money &#8212; but after covering the whole Huawei situation closely for the past several years, it\u2019s nice to see American and Chinese research facilities working together here.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2285103\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2285103\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout size-full wp-image-2285103\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-15-at-5.37.45-PM.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"708\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-15-at-5.37.45-PM.jpg 2042w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-15-at-5.37.45-PM.jpg?resize=150,104 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-15-at-5.37.45-PM.jpg?resize=300,207 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-15-at-5.37.45-PM.jpg?resize=768,531 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-15-at-5.37.45-PM.jpg?resize=680,470 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-15-at-5.37.45-PM.jpg?resize=1536,1062 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-15-at-5.37.45-PM.jpg?resize=50,35 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2285103\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Miso Robotics<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>Meanwhile, over in Miso Robotics, Flippy and Sippy meet Chippy. <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/16\/flippy-meet-chippy-chipotles-new-tortilla-chip-cooking-robot-arm\/\">R.I.P. me<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>Bear Robotics continues to ride high on funding interest amid ongoing staffing shortages. The restaurant robotics company<a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/15\/bear-robotics-targets-restaurant-staffing-shortages-with-another-81m-raise\/\"> just raised $81 million<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cHaving started my own restaurant years ago, I learned firsthand just how hard things could get,\u201d says founder\/CEO John Ha. \u201cI thought there must be a way to automate some of these repetitive tasks without losing what makes a restaurant great. That\u2019s why we created Servi. It\u2019s a solution meant to enhance the experience of customers, employees, and operators. While others are trying to fully automate work, we\u2019re trying to elevate the future of work for stakeholders in this industry that keep it going each day.\u201d<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2285030\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2285030\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout size-full wp-image-2285030\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Servi_hw55_4.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"683\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Servi_hw55_4.jpg 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Servi_hw55_4.jpg?resize=150,100 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Servi_hw55_4.jpg?resize=300,200 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Servi_hw55_4.jpg?resize=768,512 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Servi_hw55_4.jpg?resize=680,453 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Servi_hw55_4.jpg?resize=1536,1024 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Servi_hw55_4.jpg?resize=50,33 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2285030\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Bear Robotics<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>Bear says its Servi robot has thus far delivered 28 million meals over a combined 335,000 miles.<\/p>\n<p>We covered Third Wave Automation\u2019s <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/08\/04\/third-wave-automation-raises-40m-to-bring-its-autonomous-forklifts-to-warehouses\/\">$40 million Series B<\/a> last year. This week, the Bay Area firm <a href=\"https:\/\/www.businesswire.com\/news\/home\/20220316005366\/en\/Third-Wave-Automation-and-Clark-Material-Handling-Company-Announce-Partnership-and-Launch-of-a-New-Mixed-Mode-Autonomous-Forklift\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">announced a new autonomous forklift<\/a>, the TWA Reach. It\u2019s the first product resulting from a partnership with forklift maker, Clark. Per the companies, \u201cThe automated truck is most suitable for those warehouses and distribution centers looking to improve overall pallet movement productivity and operator efficiency in and around existing racking.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>If you haven\u2019t spent a lot of time around warehouses, you might be shocked by how common forklift accidents are. OSHA puts the number at 34,900 serious accidents, 61,800 non-serious and 85 deaths each year in the U.S. alone.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2284266\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2284266\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout size-full wp-image-2284266\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/ElliQ10.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"730\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/ElliQ10.jpg 2172w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/ElliQ10.jpg?resize=150,107 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/ElliQ10.jpg?resize=300,214 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/ElliQ10.jpg?resize=768,547 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/ElliQ10.jpg?resize=680,485 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/ElliQ10.jpg?resize=1536,1095 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/ElliQ10.jpg?resize=2048,1460 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/ElliQ10.jpg?resize=50,36 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2284266\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Intuition Robotics<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>At long last, the <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/15\/the-elliq-eldercare-robot-is-finally-available\/\">ElliQ eldercare robot<\/a> is finally available from Intuition Robotics. It\u2019s been several years of beta testing and multiple funding rounds since we first saw the little robot in action, and now it\u2019s finally available. The product is designed for older users who are still able to live independently, but might need a little assist. It runs $250 upfront and $30 a month.<\/p>\n<p>Over in car land, Ford wins <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/16\/ford-is-now-using-robots-to-operate-3d-printers-without-human-help\/\">hardware buzz bingo<\/a> with a robot arm designed to operate a Carbon 3D printer. As noted in our piece, robots have been helping build Ford cars for a long time now. This latest application uses KUKA robots to print small batches of custom parts, including things like a brake line bracket for Mustang Shelby GT500. They\u2019re hoping to scale things up &#8212; but, then, so is everyone in 3D printing land.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2283630\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2283630\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout size-full wp-image-2283630\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/DIAMOND_AGE_20210472.2_larger.jpg\" alt=\"House building robot\" width=\"1024\" height=\"683\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/DIAMOND_AGE_20210472.2_larger.jpg 1500w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/DIAMOND_AGE_20210472.2_larger.jpg?resize=150,100 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/DIAMOND_AGE_20210472.2_larger.jpg?resize=300,200 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/DIAMOND_AGE_20210472.2_larger.jpg?resize=768,513 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/DIAMOND_AGE_20210472.2_larger.jpg?resize=680,454 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/DIAMOND_AGE_20210472.2_larger.jpg?resize=50,33 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2283630\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Diamond Age<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>I suppose you could say Diamond Age has scaled things up in a more literal sense. The company uses its own combination of robot arms and additive manufacturing to 3D print houses. After a recent $8 million raise, it just added <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/11\/diamond-age-series-a\/\">another $50 to its coffers<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cAffordable housing is impacting people on a global scale. As the average age for first-time homebuyers has moved from mid-twenties to mid-thirties, there\u2019s an increased demand for more rental property \u2014 forcing the entire hierarchy of renters into a more competitive market for \u2018quality\u2019 housing,\u201d says co-founder\/CEO Jack Oslan. \u201cHelping the next generation of homebuyers get into their first house faster helps the entire ecosystem of housing.\u201d<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2285455\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2285455\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout size-full wp-image-2285455\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/minicheetahdog4.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"683\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/minicheetahdog4.png 4134w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/minicheetahdog4.png?resize=150,100 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/minicheetahdog4.png?resize=300,200 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/minicheetahdog4.png?resize=768,512 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/minicheetahdog4.png?resize=680,453 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/minicheetahdog4.png?resize=1536,1024 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/minicheetahdog4.png?resize=2048,1365 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/minicheetahdog4.png?resize=50,33 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2285455\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> MIT CSAIL<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>We\u2019ve got an old friend returning to close us out this week. MIT CSAIL\u2019s Mini Cheetah recently learned to run a lot faster. Says the team:<\/p>\n<blockquote><p>At the heart of artificial intelligence research is the tradeoff between what the human needs to build in (nature) and what the machine can learn on its own (nurture). The traditional paradigm in robotics is that humans tell the robot both what task to do and how to do it. The problem is that such a framework is not scalable, because it would take immense human engineering effort to manually program a robot with the skills to operate in many diverse environments. A more practical way to build a robot with many diverse skills is to tell the robot what to do and let it figure out the how. Our system is an example of this. In our lab, we\u2019ve begun to apply this paradigm to other robotic systems, including hands that can pick up and manipulate many different objects.<\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2191371\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2191371\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout size-full wp-image-2191371\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/08\/actuator-blue.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"576\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/08\/actuator-blue.jpg 3200w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/08\/actuator-blue.jpg?resize=150,84 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/08\/actuator-blue.jpg?resize=300,169 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/08\/actuator-blue.jpg?resize=768,432 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/08\/actuator-blue.jpg?resize=680,383 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/08\/actuator-blue.jpg?resize=1536,864 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/08\/actuator-blue.jpg?resize=2048,1152 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/08\/actuator-blue.jpg?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2191371\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Bryce Durbin\/TechCrunch<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p><em>Run, don&#8217;t walk to the <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/newsletters\">Actuator subscription page<\/a>. Or walk. I don&#8217;t care. 8"}]}}],"wp:term":[[{"id":449546991,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/robotics\/","name":"Robotics","slug":"robotics","taxonomy":"category","parent":0,"rapidData":{"pt":"","pct":""},"submenu_categories":[],"_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/categories\/449546991"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/categories"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/category"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?categories=449546991"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?categories=449546991"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?categories=449546991"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[{"id":1334084,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/3d-printing\/","name":"3d age","slug":"diamond-age","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576910931"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576910931"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576910931"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576910931"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576910931"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":19071,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/ford\/","name":"Ford","slug":"ford","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/19071"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=19071"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=19071"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=19071"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=19071"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":43886,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/mit\/","name":"MIT","slug":"mit","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/43886"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=43886"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=43886"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=43886"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=43886"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":13426,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/robotics\/","name":"robotics","slug":"robotics","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/13426"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=13426"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=13426"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=13426"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=13426"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":576858647,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/robotics-roundup\/","name":"Robotics roundup","slug":"robotics-roundup","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576858647"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576858647"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576858647"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576858647"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576858647"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2285724,"date":"2022-03-17T06:00:42","date_gmt":"2022-03-17T13:00:42","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2285724"},"modified":"2022-03-17T08:36:20","modified_gmt":"2022-03-17T15:36:20","slug":"mac-studio-review","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/17\/mac-studio-review\/","title":{"rendered":"Mac Studio review: emerging from the Mac&#8217;s midlife crisis"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><span class=\"featured__span-first-words\">The rumor mill<\/span> nailed most of the announcements in the lead up to last week\u2019s event. But in an era when so much of consumer hardware has grown samey, Apple still managed to surprise. In the grand scheme of event unveils, the Mac Studio wasn\u2019t a huge curveball, exactly, so much as the last sign of a company continuing to evolve its personal computer strategy. Nearly a half-century after the arrival of the first Apple computer, the category still has some life left in it yet.<\/p>\n<p>Just a few years ago, I wouldn\u2019t have felt confident in that statement. The Mac was very much undergoing a midlife crisis. The iPhone had rocketed to the top of the list both in terms of Apple mind and revenue share, and the iPad soaked up what was left. When it came to innovation, macOS was seemingly stuck with reheated leftovers from its mobile counterpart.<\/p>\n<p>On the hardware side, meanwhile, it seemed the company had abandoned the professional creative category that once formed a key segment of its base, leaving room for products like Microsoft\u2019s Surface line to blossom in its wake. It attempted to reignite some excitement around the addition of the Touchbar, but eventually even Apple had to give up the ghost, quietly phasing out that strange experiment.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2285724\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>The Macs of a few years ago suffered from bad keyboards (there were lawsuits) and a lack of ports. The latter was easy enough to chalk up to Apple streamlining, but that didn\u2019t make it sting any less.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2284057\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2284057\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout wp-image-2284057 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/CMC_0978.jpg\" alt=\"Apple iMac studio display computer desktop 2022 set up with keyboard, mouse track\" width=\"1024\" height=\"683\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/CMC_0978.jpg 6720w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/CMC_0978.jpg?resize=150,100 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/CMC_0978.jpg?resize=300,200 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/CMC_0978.jpg?resize=768,512 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/CMC_0978.jpg?resize=680,453 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/CMC_0978.jpg?resize=1536,1024 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/CMC_0978.jpg?resize=2048,1365 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/CMC_0978.jpg?resize=50,33 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2284057\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Brian Heater<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>But in 2020, the paradigm shifted again. Fittingly, it was yet another direct result of iPhone R&amp;D that brought the change. But this time it wasn\u2019t the addition of some iOS app. In the intervening years, Apple had leapfrogged Mac hardware when it shifted to its own in-house chip development for the iPhone. For most of the company\u2019s existence, it\u2019s preferred to go things alone where possible, and the development of its own first-party silicon has afforded that opportunity in profound new ways.<\/p>\n<p>It was only a matter of time before Apple followed suit on the Mac. The company wound down the first year of the pandemic by debuting the M1 chip &#8212; and with it, a trio of new Macs: the MacBook Air, Pro and Mini. The reviews were near unanimous: the Mac was back &#8212; at least from a performance perspective. As anyone who has ever remodeled a house or redesigned a website can tell you, teardowns take time, and that first round of M1 felt like a new engine in an old body.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>Last May, Apple released a new 24-inch iMac, which brought the new silicon to a new design &#8212; the first fundamental rebuild of its all-in-one in around a decade and a half. That\u2019s a lifetime or two in this world. I don\u2019t use the word \u201ccute\u201d a lot to refer to hardware devices. Cute is for bunny rabbits and babies. But also the 2021 iMac. Cute, but powerful. I\u2019ve been using the desktop as my daily driver for the better part of a year (I don\u2019t leave my apartment like I used to), and I\u2019ve never had any moments that felt like I\u2019d pushed the M1 beyond its limits.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2284059\" style=\"width: 6730px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2284059\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout wp-image-2284059 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/CMC_0992.jpg\" alt=\"Close up of iMac studio display desktop computer 2022\" width=\"6720\" height=\"4480\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/CMC_0992.jpg 6720w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/CMC_0992.jpg?resize=150,100 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/CMC_0992.jpg?resize=300,200 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/CMC_0992.jpg?resize=768,512 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/CMC_0992.jpg?resize=680,453 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/CMC_0992.jpg?resize=1536,1024 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/CMC_0992.jpg?resize=2048,1365 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/CMC_0992.jpg?resize=50,33 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 6720px) 100vw, 6720px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2284059\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Brian Heater<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>Assuming 24-inches is enough screen real estate for you, I can still heartily recommend the iMac for most users &#8212; especially for those, like me, who have space constraints. Really, my only issue on that front is going with the yellow.<\/p>\n<p>All of that said, if I had to choose, I believe I would pinpoint last October as the real birth of the modern Mac. Hear me out on this one. More than just new hardware, the<a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/10\/25\/apple-14-inch-macbook-pro-2021-review\/\"> last MacBook Pro<\/a> presents a new approach to hardware. I don\u2019t think I\u2019m talking out of school when I say that Apple has frequently been so single-mindedly focused on its own design decisions that public opinion can get steamrolled in the process. Read one of <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/09\/touch-id-forever-face-id-never\/\">Devin\u2019s impassioned essays<\/a> on the iPhone SE, and you\u2019ll see what I mean. Losing beloved features. Sometimes it\u2019s in the name of progress and sometimes for the sake of aesthetics, but it\u2019s always hard.<\/p>\n<p>Last year\u2019s Pro felt different. Our jaded staff was suitably excited when it was revealed. After years of withholding, it was a Mac that felt as uncompromising as the new M1 Pro and Max chips that powered it. It was an easy recommendation for Mac users, with none of the misgivings that had dotted other recent Mac releases.<\/p>\n<p>So, where does the Mac Studio fall in all of this? It\u2019s a bit more complicated than it appears at first blush. For one thing, as I noted up top, the product\u2019s entry was a surprise. On the desktop front, the 27-inch iMac felt like a sure bet as recently as last week. The product would be a step up from last year\u2019s all-in-one and fill the void left by the iMac Pro &#8212; a product, which in hindsight, was a stop gap as the company worked out its M1 roadmap and righted the shaky ship the Mac Pro had become.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2284044\" style=\"width: 6730px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2284044\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout wp-image-2284044 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/CMC_0957.jpg\" alt=\"Back of iMac desktop studio display 2022\" width=\"6720\" height=\"4480\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/CMC_0957.jpg 6720w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/CMC_0957.jpg?resize=150,100 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/CMC_0957.jpg?resize=300,200 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/CMC_0957.jpg?resize=768,512 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/CMC_0957.jpg?resize=680,453 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/CMC_0957.jpg?resize=1536,1024 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/CMC_0957.jpg?resize=2048,1365 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/CMC_0957.jpg?resize=50,33 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 6720px) 100vw, 6720px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2284044\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Brian Heater<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>Will there be a 27-inch iMac? Most likely, no. <a href=\"https:\/\/9to5mac.com\/2022\/03\/11\/exclusive-apple-currently-has-no-plans-to-release-a-new-larger-screen-imac\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Reports<\/a> suggest that one isn\u2019t imminent, and frankly, there\u2019s probably too much overlap with the Mac Studio. With last year\u2019s model, the iMac effectively returned to its rightful place as Apple\u2019s entry-level desktop &#8212; albeit a quite powerful one, as that bar rose across the line with the arrival of M1. Its color scheme certainly places it in the proud tradition of products like the iPod and iPhone Mini.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2284042\" style=\"width: 6730px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2284042\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout wp-image-2284042 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/CMC_0948.jpg\" alt=\"Apple Mac Studio 2022, image from the back\" width=\"6720\" height=\"4480\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/CMC_0948.jpg 6720w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/CMC_0948.jpg?resize=150,100 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/CMC_0948.jpg?resize=300,200 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/CMC_0948.jpg?resize=768,512 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/CMC_0948.jpg?resize=680,453 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/CMC_0948.jpg?resize=1536,1024 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/CMC_0948.jpg?resize=2048,1365 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/CMC_0948.jpg?resize=50,33 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 6720px) 100vw, 6720px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2284042\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Brian Heater<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>Pricing, too, is a bit more complicated than it appears at first blush. The M1 Mac Mini currently starts at $699, whereas the iMac M1 starts at $1,299. The Mac Studio, meanwhile, starts at $1,999 &#8212; effectively the price of the two products combined. Where things get a bit more complicated is that the iMac is the only device of the three that comes with its own display baked in. The upshot of that is that you don\u2019t necessarily need to go with a first-party display, if you want to save some cash or have a perfectly good screen lying around.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2285926\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2285926\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout wp-image-2285926 size-full\" href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/17\/apple-execs-on-developing-mac-studio-and-studio-display-for-the-other-pros\/\">Studio Display<\/a>, because it\u2019s the one that Apple sent us. That\u2019s going to add another $1,599 to your starting tab, which brings us to ~$3,600. Pretty soon we\u2019re going to be talking about real money here. As tested, we\u2019re talking about the M1 Max here &#8212; with the 32-core GPU, 64GB RAM and 1TB of storage, putting us at $2,799. Want the M1 Ultra? That starts at $3,999 and goes up to $7,999. At that price point, however, we\u2019re discussing the needs of &lt;.1% of Mac users here (not an actual number, mind).<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2285922\" style=\"width: 1034px\" It scored 1790\/12851 on the Apple Silicon test, versus the MacBook\u2019s 1781\/12674 and 1337\/9975 to the laptop\u2019s 1348\/9949 on the Intel version. It edged out the MacBook in the GFXBench Metal test, as well, at 307 to its 279.6. Unfortunately, we weren&#8217;t able to get our hands on the Ultra chip, but the results were extremely impressive here, nonetheless.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2285927\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Bryce Durbin\/TechCrunch<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>What&#8217;s even more impressive is the Studio was able to perform what would have been an extremely resource-intensive task on an Intel model without so much as firing up the fan or even getting warm to the touch, really.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2285925\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2285925\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout wp-image-2285925 size-full\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Bryce Durbin\/TechCrunch<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>After Apple one-more-thinged the Mac Pro at last week\u2019s event, you\u2019ve got to wonder where the company is going from here. The M2 chip? Perhaps, but even so, there aren\u2019t a ton of people who need to, say render a full Pixar film or develop really high-end VR content. Those people do exist, of course, and there will be increasingly more of them, moving forward. And hey, even more so than laptops, it\u2019s important to future-proof these devices. You\u2019re going to want a $3,000 desktop to last a while.<\/p>\n<p>Like the new Pro, there are fewer tradeoffs here than, say, on the Mac Mini. First and foremost is ports. Ports are important. They let your things connect to other things. The Studio sports a pair of USB-C ports in the front, along with an SD reader. The latter, in particular, is one you interact with frequently, so it\u2019s handy having it up front. Around the other side are two more USB-Cs, two USB-As (something I\u2019ve missed on the iMac), ethernet, a headphone jack and HDMI out (but not in). Add in the Studio Display and you get another four ports.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2284039\" style=\"width: 6730px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2284039\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout wp-image-2284039 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/CMC_0940.jpg\" alt=\"four ports of Mac Studio 2022 back of device\" width=\"6720\" height=\"4480\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/CMC_0940.jpg 6720w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/CMC_0940.jpg?resize=150,100 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/CMC_0940.jpg?resize=300,200 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/CMC_0940.jpg?resize=768,512 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/CMC_0940.jpg?resize=680,453 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/CMC_0940.jpg?resize=1536,1024 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/CMC_0940.jpg?resize=2048,1365 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/CMC_0940.jpg?resize=50,33 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 6720px) 100vw, 6720px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2284039\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Brian Heater<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>Even more so than the Studio itself, the Studio Display fills an important hole in the Apple lineup. Keep in mind, Apple completely got out of the first-party display game for some time before the arrival of the $5,000 Pro Display XDR. Like the Mac Pro or M1 Ultra, Pro Display XDR is more monitor than most people will need. If you\u2019re keen to get a first-party Apple monitor, the 27-inch, 5K Retina Apple Studio Display is plenty of screen for most. For another $300, the anti-reflective coating, coupled with nano textured glass, dramatically reduces glare, which is nice for pro and non-pro users, alike.<\/p>\n<p><!--[if lt IE 9]><script>document.createElement('audio');<\/script><![endif]-->\n<audio class=\"wp-audio-shortcode\" id=\"audio-2285724-1\" preload=\"none\" style=\"width: 100%;\" controls=\"controls\"><source type=\"audio\/mpeg\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/05\/white-noise.m4a?_=1\" \/><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/05\/white-noise.m4a\">https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/05\/white-noise.m4a<\/a><\/audio><\/p>\n<p><em>iMac 2021 mic test<\/em><\/p>\n<p><audio class=\"wp-audio-shortcode\" id=\"audio-2285724-2\" preload=\"none\" style=\"width: 100%;\" controls=\"controls\"><source type=\"audio\/mpeg\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Mac-Studio-Audio.m4a?_=2\" \/><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Mac-Studio-Audio.m4a\">https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Mac-Studio-Audio.m4a<\/a><\/audio><\/p>\n<p><em>Mac Studio 2022 mic test<\/em><\/p>\n<p>The mic quality is good &#8212; Apple\u2019s positioning them as \u201cstudio quality,\u201d but if you\u2019re planning to do much more than just webconferencing, I\u2019d recommend plugging an external mic into one of the aforementioned ports. Among other things, that will afford you the ability to get in much tighter. The speakers have fuller sound than the most recent iMac, owing in part to the wider, thicker frame that allows for more surface area for the down-firing grilles.<\/p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout alignnone wp-image-2285784 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/lBdCd1CD1.jpg\" alt=\"Clockwise from top left: iMac 2020, iMac 2021, Opal C1 external webcam, Mac Studio camera review test images\" width=\"1024\" height=\"1063\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/lBdCd1CD1.jpg 1280w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/lBdCd1CD1.jpg?resize=144,150 144w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/lBdCd1CD1.jpg?resize=289,300 289w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/lBdCd1CD1.jpg?resize=768,797 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/lBdCd1CD1.jpg?resize=655,680 655w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/lBdCd1CD1.jpg?resize=32,32 32w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/lBdCd1CD1.jpg?resize=48,50 48w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><\/p>\n<p><em>Clockwise from top left: iMac 2020, iMac 2021, Opal C1 external webcam, Mac Studio<\/em><\/p>\n<p>The biggest disappointment here from the AV perspective is undoubtedly the webcam. Center Stage does a good job tracking, but the image is a surprising step down from recent M1 Macs. The white balance is off and there\u2019s more image noise. My first instinct was to try to peel away a protective film I might have left on by accident, but to no avail. That&#8217;s just how the image is now &#8212; a pretty huge disappointment for a monitor that starts at $1,599.<\/p>\n<p>That&#8217;s exacerbated by the company&#8217;s recent insistence that users won&#8217;t need an external webcam with the new Macs, after a focus first on the M1&#8217;s ISP and then subsequent updates to the camera itself. The above image should make it evident why &#8212; for now, at least, I&#8217;m sticking with the external camera for my work interviews and podcast (the shots were taking under similar lighting conditions, but note that the Opal flips the image by default). I will happily give it another go after a fix is pushed.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2281598\" style=\"width: 1690px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2281598\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout wp-image-2281598 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/apple-march-2022-mac-studio-overview.jpg\" alt=\"Apple Studio Mac Studio overview\" width=\"1680\" height=\"944\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/apple-march-2022-mac-studio-overview.jpg 1680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/apple-march-2022-mac-studio-overview.jpg?resize=150,84 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/apple-march-2022-mac-studio-overview.jpg?resize=300,169 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/apple-march-2022-mac-studio-overview.jpg?resize=768,432 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/apple-march-2022-mac-studio-overview.jpg?resize=680,382 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/apple-march-2022-mac-studio-overview.jpg?resize=1536,863 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/apple-march-2022-mac-studio-overview.jpg?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1680px) 100vw, 1680px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2281598\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Apple<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>The camera module is effectively the <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/08\/apple-studio-display\/\">same as the one found on the new iPad<\/a>, and hopefully it\u2019s something the company will be able to fix with a system update. So much of the tuning in these systems happens on the software side.\u00a0 Matthew has spent some time with the Studio, as well, and will be discussing it as part of a larger forthcoming piece on the hardware (we&#8217;ll link back it&#8217;s live). Quoting, in part,<\/p>\n<blockquote><p>In our testing, the <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/17\/apple-execs-on-developing-mac-studio-and-studio-display-for-the-other-pros\/\">Studio Display<\/a>&#8216;s camera produces grainy, low contrast and generally poor images both locally and remotely. The images that we&#8217;re seeing are, at this time, worse than the 2021 24&#8243; iMac&#8217;s camera produces.<\/p>\n<p>I noticed the quality issues as soon as I fired up the webcam for the first time. I checked it with other devices, and noticed that it was actually slightly better if it was running from a MacBook Pro running MacOS 12.2, though still not great. Given that there was a difference, my assumption was that it appeared to be some sort of processing error. I asked Apple if the results I had were typical, and sent sample images and video of what I was seeing. After review, an Apple spokesperson told me that the system was not behaving as expected and that Apple would be making updates to address the camera&#8217;s performance.<\/p>\n<p>I do not have a timeline or any specifics on those updates, but Apple is now aware there is an issue with the Studio Display&#8217;s camera quality and they said they are working on fixes. It&#8217;s worth knowing this going into making your purchasing decisions, and could be a reason to wait to see if those updates improve the quality.<\/p>\n<p>As of now, it does not live up to the otherwise excellent performance of the display itself and the speakers, which set a new standard for in-monitor audio.<\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2281599\" style=\"width: 1690px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2281599\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout wp-image-2281599 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/apple-march-2022-mac-studio-environment.jpg\" alt=\"Mac Studio environment overview\" width=\"1680\" height=\"944\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/apple-march-2022-mac-studio-environment.jpg 1680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/apple-march-2022-mac-studio-environment.jpg?resize=150,84 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/apple-march-2022-mac-studio-environment.jpg?resize=300,169 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/apple-march-2022-mac-studio-environment.jpg?resize=768,432 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/apple-march-2022-mac-studio-environment.jpg?resize=680,382 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/apple-march-2022-mac-studio-environment.jpg?resize=1536,863 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/apple-march-2022-mac-studio-environment.jpg?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1680px) 100vw, 1680px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2281599\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Apple<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>In a world where Apple is starting to pay more attention to <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/11\/17\/beginning-next-year-apple-will-mail-you-parts-and-tools-to-fix-your-iphone-and-mac-at-home\/\">right-to-repair concerns<\/a> and <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/08\/17\/apples-sustainability-focused-impact-accelerator-invites-first-15-black-and-brown-owned-companies\/\">broadening its focus on sustainability<\/a>, user repairability feels like a missed opportunity. The ability to lift the case off and clean the fan from the inside and replace parts would likely go a ways for many users. Though Apple isn\u2019t quite ready to make that commitment on that front. Users are going to have to bring this one into an Apple authorized shop if\/when that time comes. That means that modularity and upgradability are likely to be a big distinguishing factor when the Mac Pro arrives, perhaps at WWDC.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2284043\" style=\"width: 6730px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2284043\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout wp-image-2284043 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/CMC_0950.jpg\" alt=\"Mac Studio 2022 review of device\" width=\"6720\" height=\"4480\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/CMC_0950.jpg 6720w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/CMC_0950.jpg?resize=150,100 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/CMC_0950.jpg?resize=300,200 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/CMC_0950.jpg?resize=768,512 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/CMC_0950.jpg?resize=680,453 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/CMC_0950.jpg?resize=1536,1024 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/CMC_0950.jpg?resize=2048,1365 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/CMC_0950.jpg?resize=50,33 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 6720px) 100vw, 6720px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2284043\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Brian Heater<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>As with the iMac, the Studio looks great on a desktop. The computer\u2019s industrial design most closely resembles a taller Mac Mini, with the same rounded corners and brushed aluminum. Like the best-designed Macs, it\u2019s industrial, but not cold, and looks striking next to the <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/17\/apple-execs-on-developing-mac-studio-and-studio-display-for-the-other-pros\/\">Studio Display<\/a>, which sits atop a matching aluminum stand. There are additional stand options, which allow for adjustable height ($2,299) and a Vesta Mount adapter, which lets you tilt it into portrait mode, which I know at least one TechCrunch editor would kill for as a second Tweetdeck monitor.<\/p>\n<p>And you can really go hog wild on that front, with support for up to five monitors (four over USB-C and one 4K via the HDMI). Even if you&#8217;re not in the habit of hooking five screens up to your Mac, things still up up quickly. As configured, our Studio runs $2,799. Add in the $1,899 display (gotta have that nano-textured glass) and we&#8217;re talking ~$4,700. Then maybe add in the new black keyboard with Touch ID and number pad and mouse\/trackpad ($99\/$149). It&#8217;s not for the faint of heart or the thin of wallet.<\/p>\n<p>It&#8217;s a few hundred more than the last Intel-based <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/08\/06\/apple-27-inch-imac-review\/\">27-inch iMac<\/a> I tested, and about the same as a standalone Pro Display XDR. Hey, everything is relative, right?<\/p>\n<p>Apple is no doubt kicking itself for missing the beginning of the work from home push. If the new iMac and Mac Studio would have been available in early or mid-2020, the company would have made a killing. But, then, for many folks there may never be a return to the office. For most users, I would still go with the iMac. If you edit video, music or other resource-intensive creative pursuits and have a larger budget, however, this is a terrific machine. The Mac Pro is the last question mark in the line at the moment, but the new Studio is plenty of machine for most prospective buyers.<\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/apple-march-2022-event\"><img src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/apple-march-2022-event-banner1.jpg\" alt=\"Read more about the Apple March 2022 event on TechCrunch\" \/><\/a><\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>The rumor mill nailed most of the announcements in the lead up to last week\u2019s event. But in an era when so much of consumer hardware has grown samey, Apple still managed to surprise. In the grand scheme of event unveils, the Mac Studio wasn\u2019t a huge curveball, exactly, so much as the last sign Last year, it joined the rest of the tech world in going all digital. The company is returning to the concert venue, with a &#8220;limited live audience.&#8221; Once again, the show will feature a free virtual streaming element for everyone who can&#8217;t make it.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\">\n<p lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\">Can you untangle this string? <a href=\"https:\/\/t.co\/PyiD8ZsMBQ\">https:\/\/t.co\/PyiD8ZsMBQ<\/a> <\/p>\n<p>Keep an eye on this thread for more clues. \u2193 <a href=\"https:\/\/t.co\/uaMVzn4wgp\">pic.twitter.com\/uaMVzn4wgp<\/a><\/p>\n<p>&mdash; Google Developers (@googledevs) <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/googledevs\/status\/1504140591843717121?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">March 16, 2022<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p><script async src=\"https:\/\/platform.twitter.com\/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"><\/script><\/div>\n<p>Like Apple&#8217;s WWDC, the show is developer-focused, while also front-loaded with consumer content during kick-off. Updates to Android, Wear OS and various Google services are a near-lock. Hardware has traditionally been a bit more of a crapshoot. Some years have seen no devices, while others have brought addition to the Nest and Pixel lines. The show has also contained its share of surprises, including the announcement &#8212; and subsequent first live demo &#8212; of the company&#8217;s AI booking service, Duplex.<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Feel that? meet Chippy, Chipotle\u2019s new tortilla chip-cooking robot arm"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">From the company that gave you Flippy, the hamburger-cooking robot arm, comes Chippy, which does the same for tortilla chips. Miso Robotics today announced that it has teamed with fast casual Mexican restaurant chain Chipotle to develop a system designed to deep fry and season chips &#8212; not too much of a stretch, really, after Flippy 2 figured out how to make French fries for White Castle last year.<\/p>\n<p>The new robot\/AI system is currently being tested at the chain\u2019s Cultivate Center food laboratory in Orange County. It expects to start testing Southern California restaurants at some point later this year. Like the Flippy roll out before it, the Chippy\u2019s maker will be using the testing period to determine what works &#8212; and doesn\u2019t &#8212; for employees and customers alike.<\/p>\n<p>In addition to dipping the basket into the vat of hot oil, the system is also designed to season the chips with salt and lime juice. Chipotle says a little chaos is a key to adding some humanity back into the system.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2285099\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>\u201cEveryone loves finding a chip with a little more salt or an extra hint of lime,\u201d said Nevielle Panthaky, vice president of Culinary, Chipotle. \u201cTo ensure we didn\u2019t lose the humanity behind our culinary experience, we trained Chippy extensively to ensure the output mirrored our current product, delivering some subtle variations in flavor that our guests expect.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>Chippy joins Flippy and Miso\u2019s soft drink dispenser, Sippy. Can Tippy, the serving robot or Trippy, a weed concierge robot, be far behind?<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"xNFEkHh9nP\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/11\/02\/flippy-the-hamburger-cooking-robogets-a-more-capable-successor\/\">Flippy, the hamburger-cooking robot, gets more capable<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Flippy, the hamburger-cooking robot, gets more capable&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/11\/02\/flippy-the-hamburger-cooking-robogets-a-more-capable-successor\/embed\/#?secret=pXACRIK0DQ#?secret=xNFEkHh9nP\" data-secret=\"xNFEkHh9nP\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>From the company that gave you Flippy, the hamburger-cooking robot arm, comes Chippy, which does the same for tortilla chips. uses robots to keep an eye on greenhouse crops"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Not going to lie, <a href=\"https:\/\/iunu.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">IUNU<\/a> (pronounced \u201cyou knew\u201d) is not the easiest name (further confusing matters is the presence of a robot called \u201cLUNA\u201d). But the agtech firm is involved in a solid business and just got a nice vote of confidence in the form of a Series B round. Today\u2019s news finds the Seattle-based firm picking up $24 million in funding, led by Lewis &amp; Clark Ventures, with S2G Ventures, Ceres Partners and Astanor Ventures returning for more.<\/p>\n<p>The company is targeting the world of greenhouses. Its LUNA robotic system moves along the top of a greenhouse roof, checking in on crops using computer vision. The system can detect problem areas and spots that are ready to harvest, so farmers don\u2019t have to walk up and down crops &#8212; something that starts to become an issue as farms scale.<\/p>\n<p>These are the kind of systems we\u2019ve commonly seen rolled out for more traditional farms as part of a larger autonomous robot. Greenhouses certainly make sense for the tech, as they effectively allow it to move back and forth on a track.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2285119\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>IUNU says it\u2019s currently working with a quarter of greenhouse leafy green growers in the U.S. The company currently employs 60, a 50% increase in headcount over the last six months. This round will go toward expanding its global footprint, as well as increasing R&amp;D on new products.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cThis round of investment reflects the confidence institutional investors have in us,\u201d CEO Adam Greenberg says in a release. \u201cThe conversation around autonomous growing has accelerated in the past year, and we\u2019re proud to be leading the way on this front.<\/p>\n<p>As always, data\u2019s the big play here, and IUNU claims it currently has the \u201clargest production dataset in the industry,\u201d based on existing deployment. A big cache like that is important for creating algorithms that can help identify potential problems before they become major issues for a given crop.<\/p>\n<p>In September, the company acquired our 2015 Startup Battlefield winner <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2019\/05\/22\/agtech-startup-agrilyst-is-now-artemis-raises-8m-series-a\/\">Artemis (nee Agrilyst)<\/a> to bolster its data-collecting capabilities.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Not going to lie, IUNU (pronounced \u201cyou knew\u201d) is not the easiest name (further confusing matters is the presence of a robot called \u201cLUNA\u201d). But the agtech firm is involved in a solid business and just got a nice vote of confidence in the form of a Series B round. Today\u2019s news finds the Seattle-based ar Robotics targets restaurant staffing shortages with another $81M raise"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">One of the most interesting things about following food robotics startups over the past couple of years is tracking all of the different tasks companies are looking to automate, from prep to delivery. Bay Area-based Bear isn\u2019t the only firm attempting to bring robots out in front of the the counter, but in recent years, it\u2019s become one of the most prominent.<\/p>\n<p>Bear has seen some success in deployment of late, including a bid to get its system in more restaurants in Japan. That push comes courtesy of backer SoftBank, as well as some ongoing labor shortages in the country. Japan has long eyed robots as a way to keep business moving for its aging population, and the pandemic only served to accelerate those needs. Here in the States, Bear has partnered with Chili\u2019s, Compass Group, Denny\u2019s, Marriott and Pepsi.<\/p>\n<p>The business model has clearly garnered a lot of confidence in SoftBank, which has become even more bullish on robotics of late, leading its 2020 Series A. Today new investor IMM is coming on board to lead an <a href=\"https:\/\/www.bearrobotics.ai\/blog\/the-road-to-success-is-paved-in-solutions\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">$81 million Series B<\/a>, along with existing investors like Cleveland Avenue. This latest round brings Bear\u2019s full funding up around $117 million to date.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2285022\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>Bear is understandably cautious around the subject of full automation. The company has long positioned itself as a way for restaurants to augment &#8212; rather than replace &#8212; human waitstaffs. That\u2019s no doubt, in part, due to the fact that the machines are more akin to mobile tables, rather than robot waiters, moving orders from Point A to Point B.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cHaving started my own restaurant years ago, I learned firsthand just how hard things could get,\u201d founder\/CEO John Ha said in a release. \u201cI thought there must be a way to automate some of these repetitive tasks without losing what makes a restaurant great. That\u2019s why we created Servi. It\u2019s a solution meant to enhance the experience of customers, employees, and operators. While others are trying to fully automate work, we\u2019re trying to elevate the future of work for stakeholders in this industry that keep it going each day.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>All told, Bear says its Servi robot has delivered 28 million meals over a combined 335,000 miles.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"bAscjyWB8q\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/07\/09\/5-fundraising-imperatives-for-robotics-startups\/\">5 fundraising imperatives for robotics startups<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;5 fundraising imperatives for robotics startups&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/07\/09\/5-fundraising-imperatives-for-robotics-startups\/embed\/#?secret=qVlsCttyjJ#?secret=bAscjyWB8q\" data-secret=\"bAscjyWB8q\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>One of the most interesting things about following food robotics startups over the past couple of years is tracking all of the different tasks companies are looking to automate, from prep to delivery. ch.com\/?p=2284628"},"modified":"2022-03-15T09:19:59","modified_gmt":"2022-03-15T16:19:59","slug":"bowery-is-selling-vertically-farmed-strawberries-in-limited-quantities","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/15\/bowery-is-selling-vertically-farmed-strawberries-in-limited-quantities\/","title":{"rendered":"Bowery is selling vertically farmed strawberries in limited quantities"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Every time someone moves to the East Coast, they invariably complain about the Mexican food. Understandably. It is, in a word, lacking. For me, however, it\u2019s the strawberries. I\u2019m from California, went to school in the central valley and since I moved to New York City, I haven\u2019t found a good one. Heck, I\u2019ve spoken with East Coast natives who swear strawberries are a trash fruit. Clearly the words of someone who has never eaten the fruit freshly plucked from a field in Watsonville.<\/p>\n<p>The \u201curban farmers\u201d at Bowery have been working to change that. When <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/10\/27\/bowery-tc1\/\">I visited a farm in Kearny, New Jersey last year,<\/a> the company let me try a few samples, which they\u2019d been engineering to find the perfect \u201crecipe.\u201d The results were good. Not Watsonville\u2019s size-of-a-croquet-ball good, but good. More importantly, the placement of the company\u2019s farms means the berries don\u2019t have to travel great distances to their destination &#8212; a benefit for carbon footprints and end quality of the fruit.<\/p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-2284633\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/addtext_com_MTAyMDQxNjk2NA.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"665\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/addtext_com_MTAyMDQxNjk2NA.png 1024w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/addtext_com_MTAyMDQxNjk2NA.png?resize=150,97 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/addtext_com_MTAyMDQxNjk2NA.png?resize=300,195 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/addtext_com_MTAyMDQxNjk2NA.png?resize=768,499 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/addtext_com_MTAyMDQxNjk2NA.png?resize=680,442 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/addtext_com_MTAyMDQxNjk2NA.png?resize=50,32 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2284628\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>The firm announced that its first berries are available for purchase in limited quantities as a \u201cduo-pack\u201d in select New York City retailers, including Eataly, Tom Colicchio\u2019s Craft and Jos\u00e9 Andr\u00e9s\u2019 Le\u00f1a and Spanish Diner. I should mention, before we go any further, that in spite of the roughly four years of experimentation that\u2019s been going on behind the scenes, this is still early days &#8212; hence the \u201climited edition\u201d nature. Think about it as a fruit drop, if that helps.<\/p>\n<p>Pricing is something I brought up a lot in my interviews with various Bowery folks. I firmly believe that vertical farming is going to have to &#8212; at bare minimum &#8212; compete with organic produce pricing to make a meaningful dent in the market. The duo-pack, which weighs a combined 8 oz., runs $15. Now, if you\u2019re a Michelin-star chef, perhaps that\u2019s not a deal breaker, versus the <a href=\"https:\/\/ny.eater.com\/2019\/11\/21\/20964821\/oishii-omakase-strawberry-nyc-new-jersey\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">$50 strawberries<\/a> we saw not that long ago, but a quick search on Fresh Direct puts a 16 oz. pack of organic Driscoll\u2019s strawberries at $6-8.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2284635\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2284635\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2284635\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-15-at-10.21.56-AM.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"744\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-15-at-10.21.56-AM.png 1354w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-15-at-10.21.56-AM.png?resize=150,109 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-15-at-10.21.56-AM.png?resize=300,218 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-15-at-10.21.56-AM.png?resize=768,558 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-15-at-10.21.56-AM.png?resize=680,494 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-15-at-10.21.56-AM.png?resize=50,36 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2284635\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Bowery<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>In limited quantities, novelty is no doubt a selling point. Bowery doesn\u2019t have much competition in the world of vertically farmed berries right now, so there\u2019s definitely an appeal in being among the first humans to see what the hype is all about. And the duo-pack includes different cultivars for a kind of taste test. On the right are the smaller wild-style berries and the left are the larger garden. I\u2019m just going to cut and paste Bowery\u2019s descriptions here, because I haven\u2019t tried them yet in their current form (apparently I\u2019m getting a pack tomorrow) and when it comes to writing about food my word is no good:<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<blockquote><p>Garden Berry: Intense and zesty, Bowery&#8217;s Garden Berry is the quintessential summer strawberry in one potent bite. Perfectly balanced between citrusy and sweet, these juicy yet firm ruby red berries are ideal paired with delicate whipped cream or in a bright arugula salad with a peppery vinaigrette.<\/p>\n<p>Wild Berry: Unexpected and concentrated in flavor, Bowery&#8217;s Wild Berry is petite and poppy, ideal alongside sharp cheddar, dark chocolate, or in a bitter cocktail. It is a softer, smaller, and punchy berry that packs a ton of bright, floral flavor.<\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p>As we noted, Bowery also recently acquired agtech <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/16\/following-acquisition-by-bowery-traptics-strawberry-picking-robotics-move-into-vertical-farming\/\">robotics firm Traptic<\/a> to help scale its strawberry production.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"6RguWrpr51\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/10\/27\/bowery-tc1\/\">The Bowery Farming TC-1<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;The Bowery Farming TC-1&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/10\/27\/bowery-tc1\/embed\/#?secret=UhYnDoRmdR#?secret=6RguWrpr51\" data-secret=\"6RguWrpr51\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Every time someone moves to the East Coast, they invariably complain about the Mexican food. Understandably. It is, in a word, lacking. For me, however, it\u2019s the strawberries. I\u2019m from California, went to school in the central valley and since I moved to New York City, I haven\u2019t found a good one. Heck, I\u2019ve spoken
