ElliQ eldercare robot is finally available"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">The astute TechCrunch reader will quickly note that we\u2019ve been covering Intuition Robotics for five years now, dating back to the eldercare robotics\u2019 <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2017\/02\/14\/intuition-robotics-6m\/\">crowdfunding campaign<\/a> way back in February 2017. Most of the coverage since then has found the Israeli company raising even more money <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/02\/13\/intuition-robotics-raises-36m-for-its-empathetic-digital-companion\/\">across various rounds<\/a>, without actually answering the most important question: when? Specifically, when is the ElliQ robot going on sale?<\/p>\n<p>Seems the product is finally ready for prime time. What can I say, robots take a long time, and the company has spent several years beta testing. Intuition just announced that ElliQ is officially available today, through the product\u2019s <a href=\"https:\/\/www.intuitionrobotics.com\/\">site<\/a>. As is the wont of the robotics industry in 2022, the device will be available through a subscription plan &#8212; RaaS, if you will. That starts with a $250 upfront fee and then runs $30 a month (if you go in for an annual subscription).<\/p>\n<p>Eldercare has long been a key robotics focus in Japan, but has had issues gaining a foothold elsewhere. Here in the States, a smattering of startups are getting on board, including Labrador Systems, while smart home device makers like Amazon and Google have begun building related functionality into their systems.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2284260\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2284264\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2284264\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2284264\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/ElliQ7.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"681\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/ElliQ7.png 4000w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/ElliQ7.png?resize=150,100 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/ElliQ7.png?resize=300,200 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/ElliQ7.png?resize=768,511 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/ElliQ7.png?resize=680,452 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/ElliQ7.png?resize=1536,1021 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/ElliQ7.png?resize=2048,1362 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/ElliQ7.png?resize=50,33 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2284264\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Intuition Robotics<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>I tend to think of ElliQ as something along the lines of the sadly discontinued Kuri or Jibo, focused specifically for an older audience. Rather than actually assisting with the chores like Labrador, it\u2019s designed to keep older adults engaged. The company says average users engage with the product 20 times a day for a combined 20 minutes or so. Meaning, it\u2019s not designed for the engagement level, of say, TV, but rather something more along the lines of frequent, brief check-ins.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cAfter years of hard work this day has finally come,\u201d co-founder and CEO Dor Skuler said in a release. \u201cOver the course of the pandemic, we\u2019ve seen the devastating effect that loneliness can have on the older adult population. At the same time, we\u2019ve seen ElliQ be incredibly helpful to our beta users and put a smile on their faces.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>There\u2019s a range of content available through the device, including workouts, health info from the Mayo Clinic, check-ins with loved ones and transportation through Uber Health, among other things. Effectively, assistance and engagement are the two things here for people who are independent enough to live on their own, but require a bit more help\/support.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>The astute TechCrunch reader will quickly note that we\u2019ve been covering Intuition Robotics for five years now, dating back to the eldercare robotics\u2019 crowdfunding campaign way back in February 2017. Most of the coverage since then has found the Israeli company raising even more money across various rounds, without actually answering the most important question: unlock is finally live on iPhone as iOS 15.4 arrives"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Just under a week <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/08\/apple-peek-performance-event-recap\/\">after Apple\u2019s big event<\/a>, the company dropped the latest version of a trio of operating systems: iOS\/iPadOS 15.4 and macOS 12.3 are now live. For those who don\u2019t live <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/27\/latest-apple-os-betas-deliver-face-id-with-a-mask-and-universal-control\/\">on the beta testing circuit<\/a>, that means a bunch of key features, including using Face ID with a mask unlock and <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/06\/07\/macos-12-monterey-upgrades-continuity-with-universal-control\/\">Universal Control<\/a>, which offers even more seamless integration between an iPad and Mac.<\/p>\n<p>The operating systems arrive ahead of the new iPhone SE and Mac Studio &#8212; one of which <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/14\/the-iphone-se-is-the-platonic-ideal-of-a-smartphone\/\">we just reviewed<\/a>. The whole mask unlock thing has been a pretty big bugbear for the past, oh, two years or so. Apple offered a nice stopgap solution in the form of unlocking with the Apple Watch, but this new version makes things more accessible to more users (though, again, you can always stick to the thumb with the SE).<\/p>\n<p>I\u2019ve been using the beta for several weeks and have been satisfied with the results. It works well with a mask and glasses, which was nice during the first real traveling I\u2019ve done since this whole thing started. Naturally, it struggled when my glasses fogged, but I don\u2019t know, that\u2019s probably the fault of Honeywell and Warby Parker as much as anyone. Get it together, folks. The OS will walk you through setting up the opt-in feature, while warning you that things are, naturally, safer when relying on the full face.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2284190\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2162570\" style=\"width: 1007px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2162570\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2162570\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/06\/universal-control.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"997\" height=\"566\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/06\/universal-control.png 997w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/06\/universal-control.png?resize=150,85 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/06\/universal-control.png?resize=300,170 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/06\/universal-control.png?resize=768,436 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/06\/universal-control.png?resize=680,386 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/06\/universal-control.png?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 997px) 100vw, 997px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2162570\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Apple<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>Also new on the phone side is the Tap to Pay feature, which cuts out the middleman card reader to allow iPhone users to accept payments via the NFC chip. That arrives alongside a whole bunch of new emojis &#8212; 37 in all. Included are one melting face and another peeking one, which probably didn\u2019t give its name to last week\u2019s \u201cPeek Performance\u201d event, but, really, who can say for sure anymore?<\/p>\n<p>The other big news here is on the iPadOS\/MacOS side. Apple\u2019s not positioning it as a Sidecar killer, exactly, but it will no doubt fill that role for many users. The feature makes it possible to synch keyboards, trackpads and mice between a Mac and iPad. That means you can drag and drop files between the devices and operating systems, effectively using a more seamless version of AirDrop.<\/p>\n<p>Both operating systems should be available for download now on your compatible devices.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/apple-march-2022-event\"><img src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/apple-march-2022-event-banner1.jpg\" alt=\"Read more about the Apple March 2022 event on TechCrunch\" \/><\/a><\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Just under a week after Apple\u2019s big event, the company dropped the latest version of a trio of operating systems: iOS\/iPadOS 15.4 and macOS 12.3 are now live. For those who don\u2019t live on the beta testing circuit, that means a bunch of key features, including using Face ID with a mask unlock and Universal "}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=106595"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=106595"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=106595"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=106595"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":576594957,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/mac-os\/","name":"mac os","slug":"mac-os","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576594957"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576594957"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576594957"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576594957"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576594957"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":576927346,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/mask-unlock\/","name":"mask unlock","slug":"mask-unlock","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576927346"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576927346"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576927346"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576927346"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576927346"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":576991938,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/peek-performance\/","name":"peek performance","slug":"peek-performance","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576991938"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576991938"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576991938"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576991938"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576991938"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":576978395,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/universal-control\/","name":"universal control","slug":"universal-control","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576978395"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576978395"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576978395"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576978395"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576978395"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2281828,"date":"2022-03-10T11:30:22","date_gmt":"2022-03-10T19:30:22","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2281828"},"modified":"2022-03-09T15:05:18","modified_gmt":"2022-03-09T23:05:18","slug":"as-the-worm-turns","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/10\/as-the-worm-turns\/","title":{"rendered":"As the worm turns"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><span class=\"featured__span-first-words\">Here\u2019s something for<\/span> you to mull over this fine Thursday morning: Do agtech robotics need a reset? Granted, we\u2019re dealing with a small sample size here, but a string of news items over the past year have left me wondering why the category is &#8212; thus far &#8212; failing to live up to some very strong potential.<\/p>\n<p>Warehouse fulfillment and last-mile delivery have been the real breakout stars of the pandemic &#8212; and understandably so. But given chronic labor shortages and an aging population of farmers (the average age is ~58 years in the U.S. and about a decade older in Japan), this is a huge opportunity for growth.<\/p>\n<p>There are a lot of variables, of course. The barrier for effective autonomy is certainly lower in a field than it is on a crowded city street. But there are other factors to deal with, in terms of things like computer vision and machine learning, from identifying weeds to learning to pick fragile crops like berries. There\u2019s also the question of monetization and how eager farmers will be to adopt these new technologies.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2281828\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>This has been on my mind in the wake of<a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/07\/zoox-acqui-hires-team-from-robotic-strawberry-picking-startup-strio-ai\/\"> Zoox\u2019s acquisition of Strio.AI<\/a>. I\u2019m going to be very upfront here and admit that I wasn\u2019t familiar with the latter prior to this week\u2019s news. In my defense, the company was young, having formed in 2020. In spite &#8212; or, perhaps because &#8212; of being founded during a pandemic, it managed to roll out its first prototype device quickly, testing it at farms within six months.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2168440\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2168440\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout size-full wp-image-2168440\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/06\/Zoox-in-SF.jpg\" alt=\"Zoox in San Francisco\" width=\"1024\" height=\"576\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/06\/Zoox-in-SF.jpg 2800w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/06\/Zoox-in-SF.jpg?resize=150,84 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/06\/Zoox-in-SF.jpg?resize=300,169 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/06\/Zoox-in-SF.jpg?resize=768,432 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/06\/Zoox-in-SF.jpg?resize=680,383 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/06\/Zoox-in-SF.jpg?resize=1536,864 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/06\/Zoox-in-SF.jpg?resize=2048,1152 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/06\/Zoox-in-SF.jpg?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2168440\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Zoox<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>But the acquisition effectively marks the end of Strio as a company. It was an aqui-hire, bringing over a number of employees (including the co-founder and CEO), who will be incorporated into the robotaxi team. They\u2019ll stay put in Boston, however, as Zoox is opening an R&amp;D space in that hub of robotics research. The startup\u2019s strawberry picking ambitions, however, are effectively done.<\/p>\n<p>This, of course, reflects the <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/16\/following-acquisition-by-bowery-traptics-strawberry-picking-robotics-move-into-vertical-farming\/\">recent Traptic news<\/a>. That startup is taking its strawberry-picking robots out of the fields, as it instead looks to integrate that technology into Bowery&#8217;s vertical farms. In that instance, at least, the new owner is directly incorporating the farming technology into (an albeit dramatically different) agtech setting.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_1889777\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-1889777\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout size-full wp-image-1889777\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/10\/Traptic-4.jpg\" alt=\"Traptic 4\" width=\"1024\" height=\"683\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/10\/Traptic-4.jpg 2400w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/10\/Traptic-4.jpg?resize=150,100 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/10\/Traptic-4.jpg?resize=300,200 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/10\/Traptic-4.jpg?resize=768,512 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/10\/Traptic-4.jpg?resize=680,453 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/10\/Traptic-4.jpg?resize=1536,1024 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/10\/Traptic-4.jpg?resize=2048,1365 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/10\/Traptic-4.jpg?resize=50,33 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-1889777\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Traptic<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>Then there are companies like Blue River Technologies and Bear Flag Robotics, both of which were acquired by John Deere. That\u2019s further cementing the long-time tractor maker\u2019s place at the tip of the agtech spear. Between that and the fact that it\u2019s been selling tools to farmers for nearly 200 years, John Deere\u2019s going to to be a tough company to beat. So why not just join them.<\/p>\n<p>I think that gets to the heart of the matter, really. Launching a startup is hard. That goes triple for a robotics company. In many cases, acquisition is a perfectly reasonable &#8212; or even favorable &#8212; outcome. Selfishly, it\u2019s hard to see a promising young company take themselves off the market. But can you blame them? I certainly can\u2019t. If Amazon or John Deere or whoever suddenly knocked on you door with a boatload of money and the opportunity to continue your work with a lot more resources, would you say no? Especially in the wake of what recently happened to a promising company like <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/02\/abundants-new-owner-looks-to-revive-the-apple-picking-robot-through-equity-crowdfunding\/\">Abundant<\/a>, which was the darling of agtech robotics not all that long ago.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_1831045\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-1831045\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout size-full wp-image-1831045\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/05\/ford-agility-0214_C1.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"683\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/05\/ford-agility-0214_C1.jpg 5000w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/05\/ford-agility-0214_C1.jpg?resize=150,100 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/05\/ford-agility-0214_C1.jpg?resize=300,200 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/05\/ford-agility-0214_C1.jpg?resize=768,512 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/05\/ford-agility-0214_C1.jpg?resize=680,453 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/05\/ford-agility-0214_C1.jpg?resize=1536,1024 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/05\/ford-agility-0214_C1.jpg?resize=2048,1365 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/05\/ford-agility-0214_C1.jpg?resize=50,33 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-1831045\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Ford &#8211; Agility Robotics shoot in Albany, Oreggon on May 10, 2019. <strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Courtesy of Ford\/Photo Tim LaBarge<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>As I mentioned <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/03\/putting-the-autonomous-cart-before-the-robotic-horse\/\">last week<\/a>, I <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/07\/robotics-founders-build-your-pitch-deck-around-problem-solving-not-technology\/\">recently spoke<\/a> with Agility Robotics&#8217; co-founder and CTO, Jonathan Hurst, and Playground Global\u2019s founding partner, Bruce Leak. It offered some insight into &#8212; among other things &#8212; how charmed Agility\u2019s position feels, having caught the attention of a VC fund willing to invest the time and energy into letting Agility grow and find its market. That\u2019s certainly not something anyone can assume going into this.<\/p>\n<p>Says Leak:<\/p>\n<blockquote><p>We were surfing the internet like any good venture capital group, and we ran across the video that Agility released. We were super impressed. This product, at some level, was just an incredible pair of legs. But it could walk for hours and even run across uneven terrain in a very practical way. Seeing something like that, which we thought might not even be possible, we knew we had to meet the Agility team.<\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p>What\u2019s the solution? Obviously getting more funds supercharged in the space and willing to give agtech robotics sufficient runway would be ideal. Some truly aggressive funding from the government would be a great way to own the space and take control over the U.S. food supply. Either way, I\u2019d be looking at this space a lot more closely. That strawberry is ripe for the picking, should the right robotic arm come alone.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2279807\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2279807\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout size-full wp-image-2279807\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/DoloresBakeSumGoingUp.jpeg\" alt=\"Tortoise mobile smart store selling Bake Sum goods\" width=\"1024\" height=\"874\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/DoloresBakeSumGoingUp.jpeg 3024w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/DoloresBakeSumGoingUp.jpeg?resize=150,128 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/DoloresBakeSumGoingUp.jpeg?resize=300,256 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/DoloresBakeSumGoingUp.jpeg?resize=768,656 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/DoloresBakeSumGoingUp.jpeg?resize=680,581 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/DoloresBakeSumGoingUp.jpeg?resize=1536,1311 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/DoloresBakeSumGoingUp.jpeg?resize=2048,1749 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/DoloresBakeSumGoingUp.jpeg?resize=50,43 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2279807\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Tortoise<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>On the note of finding your market comes interesting <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/04\/tortoise-pivots-away-from-robotic-delivery-towards-mobile-stores\/\">news out of Tortoise<\/a>, which is pivoting from the white-hot category of last-mile delivery to the red-hot world of autonomous retail. Here that basically means sticking a \u201cmobile store\u201d on the back of Tortoise\u2019s little robots. Fun quote from co-founder Dmitry Shevelenko here about knowing when to pivot and not looking back:<\/p>\n<blockquote><p>You have to know what hyper-growth tastes like, and you have to have the humility to know what the fake version of it tastes like. It\u2019s hard and it\u2019s painful to make these pivots, and you look like an idiot when six months ago you were telling the world last-mile is the next great thing, and now you\u2019re saying something else, but it\u2019s better to suffer some of the indignation of that than to keep doing the same thing and expect a different result.<\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p>Nvidia, meanwhile, wants you to know it\u2019s still invested in that last mile. The components giant <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/08\/nvidia-invests-10m-in-sidewalk-robot-delivery-company-serve-robotics\/\">just invested $10 million into Serve Robotics<\/a>, an Uber spinout that makes robots that look like Minions (tell me I\u2019m wrong).<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2281200\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2281200\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout size-full wp-image-2281200\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Serve-front-sidewalk.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"683\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Serve-front-sidewalk.jpg 4898w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Serve-front-sidewalk.jpg?resize=150,100 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Serve-front-sidewalk.jpg?resize=300,200 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Serve-front-sidewalk.jpg?resize=768,512 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Serve-front-sidewalk.jpg?resize=680,453 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Serve-front-sidewalk.jpg?resize=1536,1024 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Serve-front-sidewalk.jpg?resize=2048,1365 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Serve-front-sidewalk.jpg?resize=50,33 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2281200\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Phantom Auto \/ Post Mates \/ Serve Robotics.<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>\u201cWe see ourselves as a company that\u2019s leading with autonomy and scaling real autonomous robots out in the real world,\u201d says Serve CEO Ali Kashani. \u201cNvidia is one of the most critical companies to the robotics space as a whole, and they\u2019re also investing in the tools, so it just makes sense for us to work close together given this is a developing space.\u201d<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2281831\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2281831\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout size-full wp-image-2281831\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-04-at-4.51.38-PM-1.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"561\" https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-04-at-4.51.38-PM-1.jpg?resize=768,420 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-04-at-4.51.38-PM-1.jpg?resize=680,372 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-04-at-4.51.38-PM-1.jpg?resize=50,27 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2281831\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Gecko Robotics<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>A big <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/04\/infrastructure-is-broken-gecko-is-using-robotics-to-help-fix-it\/\">$73 million raise<\/a> for Gecko Robotics this week. Talk about places in desperate need of government funding. It\u2019s hard to ignore the fact that a bridge collapsed in the startup\u2019s hometown of Pittsburgh the same day the president arrived to talk infrastructure funding. Gecko\u2019s own technology is specifically designed to monitor manufacturing structures for categories like oil and gas, power, manufacturing and defense.<\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/08\/ges-worm-robot-sports-roach-style-whiskers-to-remove-fat-deposits-from-sewage-pipes\/\">GE\u2019s Pipe-worm<\/a> (Programmable Worm for Irregular Pipeline Exploration) robot also began life on the defense side. Specifically, the project was birthed out of DARPA\u2019s Underminer program as a way to develop tunneling technology for the military. These days, it\u2019s got a new job &#8212; and a set of cockroach-inspired whiskers, which offer tactile feedback to help it navigate around pipes and tunnels. The robot sports fluid-powered muscles that offer enough strength to unclog fat deposits &#8212; or fatbergs.<\/p>\n<p>The robot is really leaning in to the \u201cdirty\u201d part of the three robotic Ds.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2191371\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2191371\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout size-full wp-image-2191371\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/08\/actuator-blue.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"576\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/08\/actuator-blue.jpg 3200w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/08\/actuator-blue.jpg?resize=150,84 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/08\/actuator-blue.jpg?resize=300,169 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/08\/actuator-blue.jpg?resize=768,432 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/08\/actuator-blue.jpg?resize=680,383 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/08\/actuator-blue.jpg?resize=1536,864 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/08\/actuator-blue.jpg?resize=2048,1152 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/08\/actuator-blue.jpg?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2191371\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Bryce Durbin\/TechCrunch<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>Dull?<em> Never! <\/em>Dirty?<em> No way! <\/em>Dangerous? <em>Only one way to find out: <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/newsletters\">sign up for Actuator<\/a>.\u00a0<\/em><\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Here\u2019s something for you to mull over this fine Thursday morning: Do agtech robotics need a reset? {"rendered":"Zeta Surgical comes out of stealth with a $5.2M raise for image-guided surgery"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Boston-based Zeta Surgical comes out of stealth this week, with the announcement of a $5.2 million seed round. The funding, led by Innospark Ventures, follows a $250,000 pre-seed featuring Y Combinator and Plug and Play Ventures.<\/p>\n<p>The company was founded by Harvard graduates Jose Maria Amich and Raahil Sha, who currently serve as CEO and CTO, respectively. Harvard Medical School Associate Professor of Neurosurgery William Gormley serves as the company\u2019s chief medical officer. The team\u2019s mission is delivering precise surgical imaging guidance for non-invasive surgeries performed outside the operating room.<\/p>\n<p>Beginning with procedures like ventriculostomy and neuromodulation, Zeta believes its technology can help democratize such procedures by offering more precision and lowering the barrier of entry.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2259604\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>\u201cThere is this giant disconnect between the precision we have on one hand, and the complete lack of technology and precision we have for the other group of surgeries,\u201d says Gormley. \u201cThe reason for that is that lots of these are emergent, and the technology has just not been developed to take care of that group of patients. What [Amich and Sha] have brought is technology, which we can apply very quickly and with very little of a surgical team on a patient that\u2019s awakened and actually moving around. It\u2019s hard to overstate how different that is from what we\u2019re doing. It completely changes everything for that group of patients.\u201d<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2259478\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2259478\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2259478\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/IMG_0307.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"683\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/IMG_0307.jpg 4032w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/IMG_0307.jpg?resize=150,100 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/IMG_0307.jpg?resize=300,200 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/IMG_0307.jpg?resize=768,512 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/IMG_0307.jpg?resize=680,453 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/IMG_0307.jpg?resize=1536,1024 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/IMG_0307.jpg?resize=2048,1365 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/IMG_0307.jpg?resize=50,33 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2259478\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Zeta Surgical<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>The Zeta system includes a mixed reality overlay designed to help a surgeon pinpoint minimally invasive neurosurgery procedures. That\u2019s combined with an optional robotic system that utilizes an off-the-shelf Doosan robotic arm combined with proprietary tools. The team says they\u2019ve explored headsets for imaging, but believe the technology isn\u2019t yet accurate enough for such surgeries.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cWe have considered both AR and VR systems, but for the moment, we\u2019re going with the standard screen-based navigation,\u201d says Sha. \u201cSome of that is technical &#8212; AR systems don\u2019t really have the accuracy required for surgical-grade precision. We could do an AR overlay, but it wouldn\u2019t be as accurate as we need for neurosurgery.\u201d<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>The startup has completed pre-clinical studies in both Boston and Singapore as it eyes the North American and Asian Markets. The team is planning to file for approval with the FDA early this year, with hopes of launching a commercial version of the device in late summer\/early fall, if approvals go according to plan.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cThis current round is focused on two core deliverables: completing our initial set of clinical trials for the device,\u201d explains Amich. \u201cAnd the other is to take the device through FDA clearance and launch with our initial set of clinical partners, after the approval comes in. A huge part of this is completing the full development of the system, which will involve expanding our team and hiring new engineers.\u201d<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Boston-based Zeta Surgical comes out of stealth this week, with the announcement of a $5.2 million seed round. The funding, led by Innospark Ventures, follows a $250,000 pre-seed featuring Y Combinator and Plug and Play Ventures. The company was founded by Harvard graduates Jose Maria Amich and Raahil Sha, who currently serve as CEO and for Nothing and chips from a Series B"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">For Nothing, Mobile World Congress was prelude. The young hardware startup spent the show in meeting rooms, behind the scenes, discussing what came next. As <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/02\/nothing-smartphone-carl-pei\/\">we noted<\/a> during the show, the immediate answer is a smartphone, a device founder Carl Pei was happy to show off in back-door meetings with key mobile executives.<\/p>\n<p>Today, Nothing announced that it will be discussing some of its future moves at a livestreamed event on March 23. The timing certainly lines up with the \u201cby next month\u201d timeline that we noted in our recent report &#8212; heavily implying that we\u2019ll get our first real glimpse of the upcoming Android handset.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2280406\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2280406\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2280406\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Nothing_event.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"576\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Nothing_event.jpg 1920w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Nothing_event.jpg?resize=150,84 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Nothing_event.jpg?resize=300,169 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Nothing_event.jpg?resize=768,432 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Nothing_event.jpg?resize=680,383 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Nothing_event.jpg?resize=1536,864 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Nothing_event.jpg?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2280406\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Nothing<\/p><\/div><\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2280404\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>Also pointing in that direction is a healthy new funding round co-led by EQT Ventures and C Ventures to the tune of $70 million. In a release, the company notes, \u201cThe funding will be used to create new product categories in partnership with Qualcomm Technologies and its Snapdragon platform, and grow operations at its new London Design Hub, led by ex-Dyson Head of Design Adam Bates.\u201d<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\">\n<p lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\">We&#39;ve got a lot to catch up on Carl \ud83d\ude09<\/p>\n<p>&mdash; Android (@Android) <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/Android\/status\/1493730251167309829?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">February 15, 2022<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><script async src=\"https:\/\/platform.twitter.com\/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"><\/script><\/div>\n<p>Qualcomm was announced as a strategic partner for the firm last October, when Nothing also noted that it had raised a $50 million Series A extension.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>\u201cWith this round of financing, we have the fuel to realise the next phase of our vision of a seamless digital future,\u201d Pei said in an announcement. \u201cI\u2019m grateful for the support from our community and investors. Our first year was a warmup, and we can\u2019t wait to reveal what we\u2019re building at Nothing during the upcoming event.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>Pei was also photographed with Qualcomm executives during last week\u2019s event in Barcelona. Obviously the chipmaker builds components for far more than just handsets these days, but further support can be found in a Twitter exchange between Pei and the Snapdragon and Android accounts.<\/p>\n<p>The product would be Nothing\u2019s second, following last year\u2019s ear(1) headphones. As we noted in our initial report, the smartphone will share design elements with its predecessor, including some transparency in its casing.<\/p>\n<p>The unveiling kicks off 9 a.m. ET on the 23<sup>rd<\/sup>.<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>For Nothing, Mobile World Congress was prelude.
